A) Direct Connect
B) Leased line
C) Site-to-site VPN
D) Dial-up connectivity
Correct: C
Explanation: Site-to-site VPN creates encrypted tunnels over the public internet between branch offices and cloud resources, providing secure connectivity at significantly lower cost than dedicated circuits. Direct Connect/ExpressRoute provides dedicated private connectivity but is more expensive and requires physical circuit provisioning. Site-to-site VPN is the standard cost-effective solution for connecting branch offices to cloud environments when dedicated circuits are not justifiable.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.1 — Explain concepts related to the Open Systems Interconnection (OSI) reference model
Question: A network hub (repeater) operates at which OSI layer?
A) Layer 2 — Data Link
B) Layer 3 — Network
C) Layer 1 — Physical
D) Layer 4 — Transport
Correct: C
Explanation: A hub operates at Layer 1 (Physical) and simply repeats/amplifies electrical signals to all ports without any intelligence — it cannot read MAC addresses or IP addresses. A switch operates at Layer 2 and reads MAC addresses, making it the most common distractor. Hubs create a single collision domain and are obsolete in modern networks, replaced by switches.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.2 — Compare and contrast networking appliances, applications, and functions
Question: Which type of IDS/IPS detection method identifies threats by looking for deviations from a baseline of normal network behavior?
A) Signature-based detection
B) Anomaly-based detection
C) Policy-based detection
D) Heuristic-based detection
Correct: B
Explanation: Anomaly-based detection establishes a baseline of normal network behavior and alerts on deviations from that baseline, enabling detection of unknown (zero-day) threats. Signature-based detection matches traffic against known attack patterns and cannot detect new, unknown threats — it is the primary distractor. Anomaly detection can generate more false positives but is essential for detecting novel attacks.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.3 — Summarize connectors and cabling
Question: Which fiber optic cable type is used for shorter distances within a building and is identified by its larger core diameter?
A) Single-mode fiber (SMF)
B) Plenum fiber
C) Multimode fiber (MMF)
D) OM1 single-mode fiber
Correct: C
Explanation: Multimode fiber (MMF) has a larger core (50 or 62.5 microns) that allows multiple modes of light to propagate, making it suitable for shorter distances (up to 550 meters for OM3/OM4) within buildings and campuses at lower cost. Single-mode fiber has a 9-micron core and is used for long-distance transmission — it is the primary distractor. OM3 and OM4 are high-performance multimode fiber types commonly used with 10GbE and 40GbE laser sources.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Configure a subnet and use appropriate IP addressing
Question: A host is assigned the IP address 172.25.10.50/20. What is the network address of this subnet?
A) 172.25.10.0
B) 172.25.0.0
C) 172.25.16.0
D) 172.25.8.0
Correct: B
Explanation: A /20 mask means 20 bits for the network, with the interesting octet being the third octet. 255.255.240.0 is the /20 mask; 240 in binary is 11110000, so the network boundary increments by 16. Starting from 0: 172.25.0.0, 172.25.16.0, 172.25.32.0, etc. Since 10 is between 0 and 16, the subnet is 172.25.0.0/20. Option C (172.25.16.0) is the next subnet boundary, not the network containing .10. The /20 subnets in the third octet are: 0, 16, 32, 48, 64, etc.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.5 — Common ports, protocols, services, and traffic types
Question: A technician needs to copy a file securely between two Linux servers using an encrypted protocol. Which protocol and port should be used?
A) FTP — TCP port 21
B) TFTP — UDP port 69
C) SCP/SFTP — TCP port 22
D) Telnet — TCP port 23
Correct: C
Explanation: SCP (Secure Copy Protocol) and SFTP (SSH File Transfer Protocol) both operate over SSH on TCP port 22, providing encrypted file transfers. Standard FTP uses port 21 and is unencrypted, making it a common answer but insecure. SCP and SFTP are the standard methods for secure file transfer between Linux/Unix systems and are preferred over FTP in all modern environments.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.6 — Use the appropriate network tool or command
Question: A technician needs to test connectivity to a remote host on a specific UDP port. Which command can be used since ping only tests ICMP?
A) tracert
B) nmap -sU
C) ipconfig
D) arp -a
Correct: B
Explanation: Nmap with the -sU flag performs UDP port scanning, testing whether specific UDP ports are open on remote hosts. Ping uses ICMP and cannot test UDP ports. UDP scanning is more challenging than TCP scanning because UDP is connectionless and many firewalls silently drop UDP packets, making nmap -sU essential for UDP service verification.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.7 — Basic corporate and datacenter network architecture
Question: Which network design principle requires that there be no single point of failure in the core layer?
A) Virtualization
B) Redundancy
C) Segmentation
D) Load balancing
Correct: B
Explanation: Redundancy in the core layer ensures high availability by deploying duplicate core switches, uplinks, and power supplies so that the failure of any single component does not disrupt network service. Load balancing distributes traffic but is not specifically about eliminating single points of failure. Core layer redundancy is typically achieved using dual core switches with redundant physical links and routing protocols like OSPF.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.8 — Summarize cloud concepts and connectivity options
Question: Which cloud computing characteristic ensures that resources are available to customers on-demand without requiring pre-approval or human interaction with the service provider?
A) Broad network access
B) On-demand self-service
C) Resource pooling
D) Measured service
Correct: B
Explanation: On-demand self-service is an NIST-defined essential characteristic of cloud computing, where customers can provision computing resources automatically through a self-service portal without requiring interaction with the cloud provider. Broad network access refers to availability via standard mechanisms over the network. On-demand self-service is what distinguishes cloud from traditional hosting where provisioning required manual provider involvement.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.1 — Explain concepts related to the Open Systems Interconnection (OSI) reference model
Question: Which statement BEST describes the concept of encapsulation in networking?
A) Removing headers and trailers as data moves up the OSI stack
B) Adding protocol headers and trailers at each layer as data moves down the OSI stack
C) Encrypting data before transmission over an unsecured network
D) Converting analog signals to digital format at the Physical layer
Correct: B
Explanation: Encapsulation is the process of adding protocol-specific headers (and sometimes trailers) at each OSI layer as data moves downward from the Application layer toward the Physical layer for transmission. The reverse process (removing headers moving up the stack) is called decapsulation. Each encapsulation header contains the information needed by the peer layer on the receiving device to properly process the data.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.2 — Compare and contrast networking appliances, applications, and functions
Question: What distinguishes a Layer 3 switch from a traditional Layer 2 switch?
A) A Layer 3 switch supports 10GbE while a Layer 2 switch only supports 1GbE
B) A Layer 3 switch can perform IP routing between VLANs in addition to Layer 2 switching
C) A Layer 3 switch manages wireless access points while a Layer 2 switch only manages wired ports
D) A Layer 3 switch requires fiber connections while a Layer 2 switch supports copper
Correct: B
Explanation: A Layer 3 switch combines the high-speed port density of a switch with the IP routing capability of a router, enabling inter-VLAN routing without a separate router device. Standard Layer 2 switches only forward frames based on MAC addresses and cannot route between different IP subnets (VLANs). Layer 3 switches are commonly used at the distribution layer to provide high-performance inter-VLAN routing.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.3 — Summarize connectors and cabling
Question: What is the maximum data rate supported by Cat 5e cable?
A) 100 Mbps
B) 10 Gbps
C) 1 Gbps
D) 10 Mbps
Correct: C
Explanation: Cat 5e (enhanced Cat 5) supports 1 Gbps (1000BASE-T) Ethernet over distances up to 100 meters with a bandwidth of 100 MHz. Cat 5 (non-enhanced) supports only 100 Mbps — making 100 Mbps the primary distractor since it's easy to confuse Cat 5 and Cat 5e. Cat 5e was designed to reduce crosstalk compared to Cat 5 and remains widely installed in existing buildings.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Configure a subnet and use appropriate IP addressing
Question: An IPv6 address is written as 2001:0db8:0000:0000:0000:0000:0000:0001. What is the correctly compressed form?
A) 2001:db8::1
B) 2001:db8:0:0:0:0:0:1
C) 2001:0db8::0001
D) 2001:db8:0000::0001
Correct: A
Explanation: IPv6 address compression uses two rules: leading zeros within each 16-bit group can be removed, and one or more consecutive groups of all zeros can be replaced with ::. Removing leading zeros gives 2001:db8:0:0:0:0:0:1, and replacing the consecutive zero groups with :: gives 2001:db8::1. Option B only applies the first rule (removing leading zeros) but does not apply the :: compression, so it is partially correct but not the fully compressed form.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.5 — Common ports, protocols, services, and traffic types
Question: A network capture shows traffic on UDP port 69. Which protocol is most likely in use?
A) DHCP
B) SNMP
C) TFTP
D) DNS
Correct: C
Explanation: TFTP (Trivial File Transfer Protocol) uses UDP port 69 and is a simplified file transfer protocol commonly used for transferring configuration files to network devices and booting thin clients via PXE. DNS uses UDP port 53 and DHCP uses UDP ports 67/68 — both are UDP-based protocols that might be confused with TFTP. TFTP has no authentication or encryption, so it is only used in trusted environments.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.6 — Use the appropriate network tool or command
Question: On a Linux system, which modern replacement for ifconfig is used to display and configure network interfaces?
A) ipconfig
B) route
C) ip address (ip a)
D) netstat
Correct: C
Explanation: The ip command (specifically "ip address" or "ip a") is the modern replacement for ifconfig on Linux systems and is included in the iproute2 package. Ipconfig is the Windows equivalent, not a Linux command. The ip command also replaces the route command for routing table management (ip route) and the arp command (ip neigh), making it the unified tool for Linux network management.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.7 — Basic corporate and datacenter network architecture
Question: In VLAN design, what is the purpose of a native VLAN on an 802.1Q trunk?
A) The native VLAN carries management traffic and cannot be changed
B) The native VLAN carries untagged traffic on the trunk link
C) The native VLAN is the only VLAN that can be routed between subnets
D) The native VLAN provides encryption for trunk traffic
Correct: B
Explanation: The native VLAN on an 802.1Q trunk carries frames that arrive without a VLAN tag, ensuring backward compatibility with devices that don't support 802.1Q. By default, the native VLAN is VLAN 1, but best security practice is to change it to an unused VLAN. VLAN 1 as the native VLAN is a security risk because untagged management traffic from legacy devices could be associated with it.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.8 — Summarize cloud concepts and connectivity options
Question: Which term describes the ability of cloud infrastructure to grow capacity by adding more resources (scaling out) to handle increased demand?
A) Elasticity
B) High availability
C) Fault tolerance
D) Scalability
Correct: D
Explanation: Scalability refers to the ability to increase capacity to meet growing demand, whether by scaling out (adding more instances) or scaling up (increasing resource size). Elasticity includes both scaling up AND down dynamically in response to real-time demand changes, which is slightly different from simple scalability. Cloud scalability is one of the key economic advantages over on-premises infrastructure where capacity must be provisioned for peak demand.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.1 — Explain concepts related to the Open Systems Interconnection (OSI) reference model
Question: Which OSI layer is responsible for providing services directly to end-user applications, such as email, file transfer, and web browsing?
A) Layer 6 — Presentation
B) Layer 5 — Session
C) Layer 4 — Transport
D) Layer 7 — Application
Correct: D
Explanation: Layer 7 (Application) is the topmost layer of the OSI model and provides network services directly to user applications, including protocols like HTTP, FTP, SMTP, DNS, and SNMP. Layer 6 (Presentation) handles data formatting and encryption but does not directly interface with user applications. The Application layer does not refer to the application itself (like Chrome or Outlook), but to the protocols that support those applications.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.2 — Compare and contrast networking appliances, applications, and functions
Question: A reverse proxy server is primarily deployed to:
A) Hide internal client IP addresses from external web servers
B) Accept internet requests on behalf of backend servers and distribute them internally
C) Filter outbound web browsing for internal employees
D) Provide VPN access for remote workers
Correct: B
Explanation: A reverse proxy sits in front of backend servers and accepts incoming requests from the internet, forwarding them to internal servers while hiding the backend server details from external clients. A forward proxy hides internal client addresses from external servers — the common distractor since both proxy types provide IP address concealment but in opposite directions. Reverse proxies also provide load balancing, SSL termination, and caching for backend web servers.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.3 — Summarize connectors and cabling
Question: Riser-rated cable (CMR) is designed for use in which building location?
A) Air-handling spaces above drop ceilings
B) Vertical shafts and conduits running between building floors
C) Outdoor direct burial applications
D) Underwater conduit installations
Correct: B
Explanation: Riser-rated (CMR - Communications Multipurpose Cable, Riser) cable is rated for installation in vertical shafts and conduits between floors, where fire could spread by drawing cables upward through the building. Plenum-rated cable is required in air-handling spaces (ceiling plenums), not riser-rated cable. Riser cable is less expensive than plenum cable but must not be installed in plenum spaces where plenum cable is required.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Configure a subnet and use appropriate IP addressing
Question: Which technology allows multiple private IP addresses to share a single public IP address by differentiating sessions using unique source port numbers?
A) NAT (one-to-one)
B) DHCP
C) PAT (NAT overload)
D) Proxy ARP
Correct: C
Explanation: PAT (Port Address Translation), also called NAT overload, maps multiple private IP addresses to a single public IP address by assigning unique source port numbers to each session, allowing thousands of internal hosts to share one public IP. One-to-one NAT (static NAT) maps each private IP to a unique public IP and does not allow sharing. PAT is the form of NAT used in virtually all home and small business routers.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.5 — Common ports, protocols, services, and traffic types
Question: Which well-known port does POP3 use to retrieve email from a mail server?
A) TCP port 25
B) TCP port 143
C) TCP port 110
D) TCP port 587
Correct: C
Explanation: POP3 (Post Office Protocol version 3) uses TCP port 110 to retrieve email from a mail server, typically downloading and deleting messages from the server. TCP port 143 is IMAP and TCP port 25 is SMTP — all email protocols that are commonly confused. TCP port 995 is POP3S (POP3 over SSL/TLS), the secure version of POP3.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.6 — Use the appropriate network tool or command
Question: Which command would a technician use to renew a DHCP lease on a Windows computer?
A) ipconfig /flushdns
B) ipconfig /release then ipconfig /renew
C) ipconfig /all
D) netstat -r
Correct: B
Explanation: To renew a DHCP lease on Windows, the technician must first use ipconfig /release to release the current lease, then ipconfig /renew to request a new lease from the DHCP server. Ipconfig /flushdns clears the DNS cache (different function), and is the most common wrong answer since both use ipconfig. This two-step process is commonly used when troubleshooting IP address conflicts or after changing network segments.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.7 — Basic corporate and datacenter network architecture
Question: Which protocol is used to prevent switching loops in a network with redundant switch connections?
A) OSPF
B) EIGRP
C) STP (Spanning Tree Protocol)
D) HSRP
Correct: C
Explanation: Spanning Tree Protocol (STP) and its successors (RSTP, MSTP) prevent Layer 2 switching loops in networks with redundant paths by blocking certain switch ports, ensuring only one active path exists at a time. OSPF and EIGRP are Layer 3 routing protocols that prevent routing loops but not switching loops. STP elects a root bridge and blocks redundant paths, activating them automatically if the primary path fails.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.8 — Summarize cloud concepts and connectivity options
Question: A company subscribes to a cloud service where they develop and deploy their own custom web application without managing servers or operating systems. This is an example of:
A) IaaS
B) SaaS
C) DaaS
D) PaaS
Correct: D
Explanation: PaaS (Platform as a Service) provides a managed development and deployment platform where customers deploy their own applications without managing the underlying infrastructure or OS. IaaS requires the customer to manage the OS, which is more work than deploying an application to a managed platform. PaaS enables developers to focus entirely on writing code while the cloud provider manages patching, scaling, and infrastructure.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.1 — Explain concepts related to the Open Systems Interconnection (OSI) reference model
Question: SSL and TLS encryption protocols primarily operate at which OSI layer?
A) Layer 4 — Transport
B) Layer 7 — Application
C) Layer 3 — Network
D) Layer 6 — Presentation
Correct: D
Explanation: SSL/TLS operates at Layer 6 (Presentation) because it provides data encryption and decryption services — a presentation layer function — transparently to applications above it. Layer 4 (Transport) is a common distractor because TLS is often associated with TCP, and the acronym includes "Transport," but TLS provides presentation-layer encryption, not transport-layer functions. HTTPS, for example, is HTTP (Layer 7) encrypted by TLS (Layer 6) over TCP (Layer 4).

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.2 — Compare and contrast networking appliances, applications, and functions
Question: Which appliance provides Unified Threat Management (UTM) functionality?
A) A device that only performs stateless packet filtering
B) A single appliance that combines multiple security functions including firewall, IPS, VPN, and content filtering
C) A dedicated load balancer with SSL offloading
D) A network switch with port security enabled
Correct: B
Explanation: UTM (Unified Threat Management) appliances integrate multiple security functions — including stateful firewall, IPS, VPN, antivirus, and content filtering — into a single device, simplifying management for small to mid-sized organizations. A traditional firewall only filters traffic based on rules, whereas UTM adds inspection and protection capabilities. UTM is particularly popular with SMBs because it reduces the cost and complexity of maintaining multiple separate security appliances.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.3 — Summarize connectors and cabling
Question: Which cable type supports the highest data rate over the shortest maximum distance and is designed specifically for data center use?
A) Cat 6
B) Cat 6a
C) Cat 7
D) Cat 8
Correct: D
Explanation: Cat 8 supports 40 Gbps at frequencies up to 2000 MHz over a maximum distance of 30 meters, making it the highest-rated copper cable but limited to short data center connections. Cat 6a supports 10 Gbps over 100 meters, which makes it better for longer runs. Cat 8's extremely high performance over short distances makes it ideal for server-to-top-of-rack-switch connections in data centers.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.4 — Configure a subnet and use appropriate IP addressing
Question: What class of IPv4 address has a first octet range of 192-223 and a default subnet mask of 255.255.255.0?
A) Class A
B) Class B
C) Class C
D) Class D
Correct: C
Explanation: Class C addresses have a first octet range of 192-223, a default /24 (255.255.255.0) subnet mask, and a maximum of 254 usable hosts per network. Class B has a range of 128-191 with a default /16 mask, and Class A has a range of 1-126 with a default /8 mask. Class D (224-239) is reserved for multicast and does not use traditional subnet masks.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.5 — Common ports, protocols, services, and traffic types
Question: Which of the following is a connection-oriented protocol that guarantees delivery through acknowledgments and retransmissions?
A) UDP
B) ICMP
C) TCP
D) IP
Correct: C
Explanation: TCP (Transmission Control Protocol) is connection-oriented, establishing a connection via a three-way handshake and guaranteeing reliable, ordered delivery through sequence numbers, acknowledgments, and retransmission of lost packets. UDP is connectionless and provides no delivery guarantee — the most common distractor since both are Layer 4 protocols. TCP's reliability comes at the cost of higher overhead compared to UDP.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.6 — Use the appropriate network tool or command
Question: A technician wants to determine which process on a Windows server is listening on TCP port 443. Which command would provide this information?
A) ipconfig /all
B) arp -a
C) netstat -ano
D) tracert 443
Correct: C
Explanation: The command netstat -ano on Windows shows all active connections and listening ports (-a), in numeric format (-n), with the owning Process ID (-o), allowing the technician to identify which PID is using port 443 and then look it up in Task Manager. Ipconfig only shows IP configuration and arp shows MAC-to-IP mappings — neither shows process-to-port associations. On Linux, the equivalent command is ss -tlnp or netstat -tlnp.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.7 — Basic corporate and datacenter network architecture
Question: North-south traffic in a traditional enterprise data center primarily refers to:
A) Traffic between servers on the same network segment
B) Traffic flowing between servers in different VLANs
C) Traffic flowing between external clients and internal servers across the perimeter
D) Traffic flowing between two data centers in different geographic locations
Correct: C
Explanation: North-south traffic flows between external clients (internet users) and internal servers, crossing the network perimeter — it is the vertical flow through the data center architecture. East-west traffic flows laterally between servers within the data center. Traditional three-tier architectures were optimized for north-south client-to-server traffic, which is why they struggle with modern workloads that generate heavy east-west server-to-server traffic.

Domain: 1.0 Networking Concepts
Sub-objective: 1.8 — Summarize cloud concepts and connectivity options
Question: Which of the following BEST describes the "broad network access" characteristic of cloud computing?
A) Cloud resources can scale to meet any level of demand
B) Cloud services are accessible over the network via standard mechanisms from diverse client platforms
C) Cloud infrastructure is shared among multiple tenants
D) Cloud resources are provisioned without human interaction
Correct: B
Explanation: Broad network access, as defined by NIST, means cloud capabilities are available over the network and accessed through standard mechanisms (web browsers, APIs) from diverse client platforms including smartphones, tablets, laptops, and workstations. Scalability to meet demand is elasticity, and infrastructure sharing among tenants is multitenancy. Broad network access ensures cloud services are platform-agnostic and location-independent.
Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A network administrator is designing a small office network where every device connects to a central switch. Which topology best describes this design?
A) Bus
B) Ring
C) Star
D) Mesh
Correct: C
Explanation: In a star topology, all devices connect to a central device such as a switch or hub, making the switch the single point of connectivity. A mesh topology would require direct links between every device, which is far more cabling-intensive. Star is the dominant topology in modern Ethernet LANs because it simplifies troubleshooting and isolates failures to individual links.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which topology provides the highest redundancy by connecting every node directly to every other node?
A) Partial mesh
B) Full mesh
C) Star
D) Ring
Correct: B
Explanation: Full mesh topology creates a direct link between every pair of nodes, eliminating any single point of failure and providing the maximum number of redundant paths. Partial mesh connects only some nodes directly, reducing cost but also reducing redundancy. Full mesh is commonly used in WAN core networks where uptime is critical, though it scales poorly due to the n(n-1)/2 link requirement.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A legacy Token Ring network uses which physical topology for frame transmission?
A) Bus
B) Star
C) Ring
D) Mesh
Correct: C
Explanation: Token Ring networks pass a token sequentially around a logical ring, so each device receives and retransmits frames to the next device in the ring. Bus topology uses a single shared cable where all devices tap into the same medium simultaneously. Understanding ring topology is useful for recognizing older LAN technologies and for understanding SONET/SDH carrier rings still used in some WAN designs.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A small startup has five employees who share files directly between their laptops without a dedicated server. This arrangement is an example of which network model?
A) Client-server
B) Peer-to-peer
C) Hierarchical
D) Three-tier
Correct: B
Explanation: In a peer-to-peer network, each device acts as both a client and a server, sharing resources directly without a centralized server. Client-server networks use dedicated servers to centralize resources and authentication, which provides better scalability and security. Peer-to-peer is practical for very small environments but becomes difficult to manage as the number of users grows.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which network type is specifically designed to provide high-speed block-level storage access to servers using protocols such as Fibre Channel or iSCSI?
A) WAN
B) MAN
C) SAN
D) CAN
Correct: C
Explanation: A Storage Area Network (SAN) is a dedicated high-speed network that connects servers to shared storage devices, providing block-level access as if the storage were locally attached. A WAN connects geographically dispersed sites and is not optimized for storage traffic. SANs are commonly found in data centres where multiple servers need to access the same storage pool for virtualization or database workloads.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A university connects all buildings on its campus using fibre optic cabling spanning several kilometres but does not extend beyond the campus grounds. Which network type is this?
A) WAN
B) LAN
C) CAN
D) MAN
Correct: C
Explanation: A Campus Area Network (CAN) spans multiple buildings within a single campus or organizational site, larger than a LAN but geographically limited to one location. A MAN (Metropolitan Area Network) covers a city or metropolitan region and typically involves service provider infrastructure. CAN is the correct classification because the network is self-contained within one organization's campus.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A service provider offers Layer 2 Ethernet connectivity between customer sites across a metropolitan area at speeds up to 10 Gbps. Which WAN technology is this?
A) PPPoE
B) Metro Ethernet
C) MPLS
D) DMVPN
Correct: B
Explanation: Metro Ethernet extends Ethernet services over a metropolitan area, allowing customers to use standard Ethernet interfaces and protocols between geographically separated sites. MPLS is a label-switching technology that can carry multiple Layer 3 protocols and is typically used for larger, more complex WAN services. Metro Ethernet is attractive because it leverages familiar Ethernet technology while providing high-bandwidth city-wide connectivity.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which WAN technology uses software-defined principles to centrally manage and route traffic across multiple underlying transport connections such as MPLS and broadband?
A) Metro Ethernet
B) DMVPN
C) SD-WAN
D) PPPoE
Correct: C
Explanation: SD-WAN (Software-Defined Wide Area Network) uses a centralized controller to dynamically route traffic across multiple WAN links based on application policy and real-time link conditions. DMVPN creates a dynamic mesh of VPN tunnels but does not provide the same centralized application-aware routing. SD-WAN allows organizations to use lower-cost broadband connections alongside MPLS while maintaining application performance.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: An enterprise needs to create a dynamic, scalable IPsec VPN overlay that allows spoke sites to communicate directly with each other without routing all traffic through a central hub. Which technology meets this requirement?
A) PPPoE
B) DMVPN
C) Metro Ethernet
D) SD-WAN
Correct: B
Explanation: DMVPN (Dynamic Multipoint VPN) allows spoke routers to form on-demand IPsec tunnels directly to other spokes using NHRP, avoiding the need to route all traffic through a hub. PPPoE is a DSL encapsulation protocol used for last-mile broadband access, not enterprise VPN overlays. DMVPN is especially valuable for large branch deployments where building static point-to-point VPNs to every site would be impractical.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which WAN technology encapsulates PPP frames within Ethernet frames and is commonly used by ISPs for DSL broadband subscriber authentication?
A) MPLS
B) Metro Ethernet
C) PPPoE
D) SD-WAN
Correct: C
Explanation: PPPoE (Point-to-Point Protocol over Ethernet) encapsulates PPP within Ethernet, enabling ISPs to use PPP authentication (PAP, CHAP) over DSL and other broadband connections. MPLS operates at Layer 2.5 using labels for packet forwarding and is used within provider cores, not for subscriber authentication. PPPoE remains common in residential DSL deployments because it supports per-user authentication and IP address assignment.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which IoT wireless technology operates in the 900 MHz band, provides a range of up to 100 metres, and uses a mesh topology to connect smart home devices?
A) NFC
B) Zigbee
C) Z-Wave
D) Bluetooth
Correct: C
Explanation: Z-Wave operates in the sub-GHz 908.42 MHz band (in North America), supports mesh networking, and is specifically designed for low-bandwidth smart home automation with ranges up to approximately 100 metres. Zigbee also supports mesh networking but operates in the 2.4 GHz band rather than 900 MHz. Z-Wave's use of a dedicated frequency band helps avoid interference with Wi-Fi and Bluetooth devices.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A warehouse management system uses small tags attached to inventory items that can be scanned from several metres away without line of sight. Which technology is being used?
A) NFC
B) Bluetooth
C) RFID
D) Zigbee
Correct: C
Explanation: RFID (Radio Frequency Identification) uses electromagnetic fields to automatically identify and track tags attached to objects and can operate at ranges from centimetres to several metres depending on the frequency band. NFC is a subset of RFID but is limited to very short ranges (under 20 cm) and requires near-contact. RFID is widely deployed in supply chain, asset tracking, and access control applications.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A user taps their smartphone against a payment terminal to complete a contactless purchase. Which wireless technology enables this transaction?
A) Zigbee
B) Z-Wave
C) Bluetooth
D) NFC
Correct: D
Explanation: NFC (Near Field Communication) operates at 13.56 MHz with a maximum range of approximately 20 centimetres, making it ideal for secure contactless payments and data exchange that requires physical proximity. Bluetooth operates at much longer ranges (up to 10 metres or more) and is not suitable for the inherently short-range security model of payment transactions. NFC's very short range provides an inherent physical security benefit by requiring deliberate proximity.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which IoT technology operates in the 2.4 GHz band, supports mesh networking with up to 65,000 nodes, and is commonly used in building automation and smart energy systems?
A) Z-Wave
B) NFC
C) Zigbee
D) Bluetooth
Correct: C
Explanation: Zigbee (IEEE 802.15.4) operates in the 2.4 GHz band globally, supports mesh topologies with up to 65,000 devices per network, and is designed for low-power, low-data-rate IoT applications. Z-Wave supports far fewer nodes (up to 232) and operates at sub-GHz frequencies. Zigbee's large node count makes it suitable for large-scale building automation deployments such as smart lighting and HVAC control.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: An administrator is designing a WAN where the service provider uses label-switching to forward packets, enabling traffic engineering and support for multiple VPNs across the same infrastructure. Which technology is described?
A) PPPoE
B) MPLS
C) Metro Ethernet
D) DMVPN
Correct: B
Explanation: MPLS (Multiprotocol Label Switching) inserts short fixed-length labels between Layer 2 and Layer 3 headers, allowing routers to make forwarding decisions based on labels rather than IP routing lookups, which enables traffic engineering and Layer 3 VPN services. Metro Ethernet provides Ethernet-based connectivity but does not inherently use label switching for traffic engineering. MPLS is the dominant technology in service provider cores because of its flexibility in supporting multiple services over a single infrastructure.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A personal area network connects a smartphone to wireless earbuds and a smartwatch over a short range of up to 10 metres. Which technology is most likely being used?
A) Zigbee
B) Z-Wave
C) NFC
D) Bluetooth
Correct: D
Explanation: Bluetooth is designed for PAN (Personal Area Network) use, operating in the 2.4 GHz band with typical ranges of up to 10 metres (Class 2 devices), making it ideal for connecting personal devices. Zigbee also operates at 2.4 GHz but is intended for large-scale IoT mesh deployments, not personal device pairing. Bluetooth's widespread adoption in consumer electronics and standardized pairing mechanisms make it the de facto standard for personal device connectivity.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which network type uses licensed cellular frequencies (4G LTE or 5G) to connect IoT sensors in remote locations where wired infrastructure is unavailable?
A) Zigbee
B) Z-Wave
C) Cellular
D) NFC
Correct: C
Explanation: Cellular IoT technologies (including LTE-M and NB-IoT on 4G, and expanding with 5G) use licensed spectrum to provide wide-area connectivity for devices in locations without Wi-Fi or wired access. Zigbee and Z-Wave are short-range mesh technologies unsuitable for remote field deployments. Cellular IoT is commonly used for smart meters, asset tracking, and agricultural sensors that need connectivity across large geographic areas.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: In which network type would you most commonly find technologies such as T1/T3 leased lines, SONET, and Frame Relay connecting offices in different countries?
A) LAN
B) WLAN
C) PAN
D) WAN
Correct: D
Explanation: A Wide Area Network (WAN) connects geographically dispersed sites, often spanning countries or continents, and relies on service provider infrastructure such as leased lines, SONET, and packet-switched technologies. A WLAN provides wireless connectivity within a limited area such as a building or campus. WAN technologies are characterized by lower bandwidth relative to cost and higher latency compared to LANs.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A hybrid topology combines elements of which two topologies to form the majority of modern enterprise networks?
A) Bus and ring
B) Star and mesh
C) Ring and bus
D) Mesh and bus
Correct: B
Explanation: Modern enterprise networks typically combine star topology at the access layer (devices connecting to switches) with partial mesh at the distribution and core layers for redundancy, creating a hybrid star-mesh topology. Bus and ring topologies are largely obsolete in Ethernet networks. Hybrid topologies allow organizations to balance the simplicity of star connections at the edge with the redundancy of mesh connections at the core.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A metropolitan fibre provider delivers Ethernet services to business customers within a city using a ring of fibre between distribution nodes. What network type does this describe?
A) LAN
B) CAN
C) MAN
D) SAN
Correct: C
Explanation: A Metropolitan Area Network (MAN) covers a city or metropolitan region, connecting multiple buildings or organizations across a urban area using provider-managed infrastructure. A CAN is limited to a single organization's campus, while a MAN may serve multiple unrelated customers across a city. MANs often use SONET rings or Ethernet rings to provide resilient fibre-based connectivity to business customers.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A network uses a single cable to which all devices connect, with terminators at each end. A break in the cable causes the entire network to fail. Which topology is described?
A) Star
B) Ring
C) Bus
D) Mesh
Correct: C
Explanation: Bus topology uses a single shared cable (the bus) with all devices tapping into it; terminators absorb signals at each end, and a cable break disrupts all communications. Ring topology also fails on a break (unless dual rings are used), but devices connect in a closed loop rather than along a single linear cable. Bus topology was used in early 10BASE-5 and 10BASE-2 Ethernet networks but has been replaced by star topology due to its fragility.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which architecture places an organization's servers and applications in a provider-managed facility that the organization reaches over a dedicated WAN link or the internet?
A) Client-server on-premises
B) Peer-to-peer
C) Cloud/hosted
D) Three-tier
Correct: C
Explanation: Cloud or hosted architecture moves servers and services off-premises to provider-managed data centres, accessible over WAN or internet connections, shifting capital expenditure to operational expenditure. On-premises client-server keeps all infrastructure within the organization's own facilities. Cloud architecture introduces WAN dependency for internal users, making reliable, low-latency WAN connectivity critical.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A three-tier network architecture separates the network into which three layers?
A) Physical, Data Link, Network
B) Core, Distribution, Access
C) Internet, Intranet, Extranet
D) Client, Application, Database
Correct: B
Explanation: The three-tier hierarchical network model divides the network into the Access layer (connecting end devices), the Distribution layer (policy enforcement and routing between VLANs), and the Core layer (high-speed backbone). The OSI layers (Physical, Data Link, Network) describe protocol functions, not network design tiers. The three-tier model is the foundation of Cisco's hierarchical design methodology and is widely used in enterprise campus networks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A spine-leaf data centre architecture is an example of which broader topology category?
A) Bus
B) Ring
C) Full mesh
D) Partial mesh
Correct: D
Explanation: In a spine-leaf architecture, every leaf switch connects to every spine switch but leaf switches do not connect to each other and spine switches do not connect to each other, forming a partial mesh. A full mesh would require every switch to connect to every other switch, which is impractical at data centre scale. Spine-leaf provides predictable, low-latency east-west traffic patterns essential for modern virtualized workloads.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which statement best distinguishes a WLAN from a LAN?
A) A WLAN uses coaxial cable while a LAN uses fibre optic
B) A WLAN provides wireless connectivity using radio frequencies while a LAN uses wired media
C) A WLAN spans a wider geographic area than a LAN
D) A WLAN requires a dedicated storage network
Correct: B
Explanation: A WLAN (Wireless LAN) provides network connectivity via radio frequency (typically 2.4 GHz or 5 GHz) without physical cables, while a LAN uses wired media such as twisted-pair or fibre. WLANs do not span wider areas than LANs by definition; both typically cover the same local area. WLANs use IEEE 802.11 standards and share the same Layer 3 addressing space as the wired LAN they extend.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A network administrator manually enters a route to the 10.20.0.0/24 network on a router. Which type of route is this?
A) Dynamic route
B) Default route
C) Static route
D) Floating static route
Correct: C
Explanation: A static route is a manually configured route that does not change unless an administrator modifies it, providing predictable, overhead-free routing for stable network paths. A dynamic route is learned automatically through a routing protocol such as OSPF or EIGRP. Static routes are commonly used for stub networks, default routes, and situations where routing protocol overhead is undesirable.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Which route serves as the router's last resort when no more specific route matches a destination IP address in the routing table?
A) Host route
B) Static route
C) Summary route
D) Default route
Correct: D
Explanation: The default route (0.0.0.0/0) matches any destination address and is used when no more specific route exists, acting as the gateway of last resort. A host route (/32) is the most specific possible route, matching only a single IP address. The default route is critical at network edges where a single upstream path to the internet is used.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: OSPF is classified as which type of routing protocol?
A) Distance-vector
B) Path-vector
C) Link-state
D) Hybrid
Correct: C
Explanation: OSPF (Open Shortest Path First) is a link-state protocol in which each router builds a complete map of the network topology using Link State Advertisements (LSAs) and runs the Dijkstra algorithm to calculate the shortest path. RIP is a distance-vector protocol that only shares routing tables with neighbours without a full topology view. OSPF converges faster than distance-vector protocols and is free from routing loops by design because each router has a consistent topology database.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Which routing protocol is Cisco proprietary, uses a composite metric based on bandwidth and delay by default, and is classified as an advanced distance-vector (hybrid) protocol?
A) OSPF
B) BGP
C) RIPv2
D) EIGRP
Correct: D
Explanation: EIGRP (Enhanced Interior Gateway Routing Protocol) is a Cisco proprietary protocol that uses a composite metric incorporating bandwidth and delay (and optionally load, reliability, and MTU) and employs DUAL (Diffusing Update Algorithm) to maintain loop-free paths. OSPF is an open standard link-state protocol, not a hybrid. EIGRP is called hybrid because it combines features of both distance-vector and link-state protocols, including partial updates and neighbour relationships.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: BGP is the routing protocol used to exchange routing information between autonomous systems on the internet. Which routing protocol type is BGP?
A) Link-state
B) Distance-vector
C) Path-vector
D) Hybrid
Correct: C
Explanation: BGP (Border Gateway Protocol) is a path-vector protocol that makes routing decisions based on policies, path attributes (such as AS_PATH), and rules, rather than simple metrics. OSPF is a link-state protocol used within autonomous systems, not between them. BGP's AS_PATH attribute prevents routing loops between autonomous systems by listing every AS a route has traversed.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A router has two routes to the 192.168.10.0/24 network: one learned via OSPF and one via RIP. Which route will the router prefer and install in the routing table by default?
A) RIP route, because it has a lower metric
B) OSPF route, because OSPF has a lower administrative distance
C) RIP route, because RIP is a simpler protocol
D) OSPF route, because OSPF has a higher administrative distance
Correct: B
Explanation: Administrative distance (AD) is the trustworthiness of a routing source; OSPF has an AD of 110 while RIP has an AD of 120, so the router prefers the OSPF route because a lower AD indicates higher trustworthiness. Metric is used to compare routes learned from the same routing protocol, not between different protocols. When two protocols advertise the same prefix, the router installs only the route from the protocol with the lowest AD.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: What is the default administrative distance of a directly connected route?
A) 0
B) 1
C) 5
D) 110
Correct: A
Explanation: Directly connected routes have an administrative distance of 0, meaning they are considered the most trustworthy since the router is directly attached to that network. Static routes have an AD of 1, making them the next most preferred. An AD of 0 for connected routes makes sense because the router has direct knowledge of the network without relying on any external information.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: RIPv2 improves upon RIPv1 by adding which two features?
A) Link-state algorithm and OSPF compatibility
B) Classless routing (VLSM support) and authentication
C) DUAL algorithm and composite metrics
D) AS path attributes and policy-based routing
Correct: B
Explanation: RIPv2 added support for classless inter-domain routing (VLSM/CIDR) by including subnet masks in routing updates, and added MD5 authentication to prevent route injection attacks; RIPv1 supported neither. DUAL and composite metrics are features of EIGRP, not RIP. RIPv2 still uses the same 15-hop maximum and 30-second update timer as RIPv1, limiting its use to small networks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A network administrator configures a static route with an administrative distance of 200 as a backup to an OSPF-learned route with AD 110. What is this backup route called?
A) Default route
B) Summary route
C) Floating static route
D) Host route
Correct: C
Explanation: A floating static route is a static route configured with an AD higher than the primary dynamic routing protocol so it only becomes active if the dynamic route is removed from the routing table. With AD 200, the floating static route remains dormant while the OSPF route (AD 110) is present, activating only when OSPF loses the path. This technique is commonly used to provide WAN backup over a secondary link such as a 4G connection.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Route redistribution is used when a network runs multiple routing protocols. What does route redistribution accomplish?
A) It converts all routes to static routes for stability
B) It allows routes learned by one routing protocol to be shared into another routing protocol
C) It assigns equal administrative distances to all routing protocols
D) It prevents routing loops by blocking duplicate route advertisements
Correct: B
Explanation: Route redistribution enables routes learned by one routing protocol (such as EIGRP) to be injected into another routing protocol's domain (such as OSPF), allowing routers running different protocols to have end-to-end reachability. It does not convert routes to static routes; those remain dynamic within their respective protocol domains. Route redistribution requires careful metric translation and filtering to prevent routing loops and suboptimal paths.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Which QoS mechanism marks packets at Layer 3 using the DSCP field in the IP header to classify and prioritize traffic?
A) 802.1p
B) CoS
C) DSCP
D) Traffic shaping
Correct: C
Explanation: DSCP (Differentiated Services Code Point) uses 6 bits in the IP header's Differentiated Services field to classify packets into per-hop behaviours, enabling routers to apply different forwarding treatments based on the marking. 802.1p and CoS use the 3-bit Priority Code Point (PCP) field in the 802.1Q VLAN tag, which is a Layer 2 mechanism and is lost when frames leave the LAN. DSCP markings persist end-to-end across Layer 3 routed boundaries, making it the preferred QoS marking for WAN and inter-site deployments.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A technician notices that VoIP calls become choppy during business hours when large file transfers are occurring. Which QoS mechanism would best address this by delaying non-critical traffic to smooth its transmission rate?
A) Traffic policing
B) Traffic shaping
C) DSCP marking
D) Route redistribution
Correct: B
Explanation: Traffic shaping buffers and delays excess traffic to conform to a defined rate, smoothing bursts and allowing prioritized traffic like VoIP to transit without contention. Traffic policing drops or re-marks packets that exceed the defined rate immediately without buffering, which can cause more disruption to bulk transfers but does not smooth traffic. Traffic shaping is typically applied to outbound WAN interfaces to prevent large transfers from overwhelming limited uplink bandwidth.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Which QoS marking standard uses the 3-bit Priority Code Point (PCP) field within an 802.1Q VLAN tag to classify traffic at Layer 2?
A) DSCP
B) 802.1p
C) ToS
D) MPLS EXP
Correct: B
Explanation: IEEE 802.1p defines the use of the 3-bit PCP field in the 802.1Q frame header to provide eight Classes of Service (CoS values 0-7) for Layer 2 traffic prioritisation. DSCP operates at Layer 3 in the IP header and survives routing, while 802.1p markings are only visible within a Layer 2 domain. Voice traffic is typically marked with 802.1p CoS 5, while network control traffic uses CoS 7.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: OSPF uses which algorithm to calculate the shortest path through the network topology?
A) Bellman-Ford
B) Dijkstra's Shortest Path First
C) DUAL (Diffusing Update Algorithm)
D) Distance-vector Bellman-Ford
Correct: B
Explanation: OSPF uses Dijkstra's Shortest Path First (SPF) algorithm, running it against the Link State Database (LSDB) to compute a loop-free shortest path tree from each router's perspective. RIP and other distance-vector protocols use the Bellman-Ford algorithm. Dijkstra's algorithm guarantees loop-free paths because it builds a complete topology map before computing routes, unlike distance-vector protocols that rely on neighbour information.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A router running OSPF is connected to multiple areas. Which special router type connects an OSPF area to the backbone area (Area 0)?
A) Internal router
B) Backbone router
C) Area Border Router (ABR)
D) Autonomous System Boundary Router (ASBR)
Correct: C
Explanation: An Area Border Router (ABR) has interfaces in both a non-backbone area and Area 0 (the backbone), summarizing and forwarding routing information between areas. An ASBR connects the OSPF domain to external routing domains and redistributes external routes. ABRs are critical to OSPF's hierarchical design because all inter-area traffic must traverse Area 0.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Bandwidth throttling limits the maximum rate of traffic for specific applications or users. In which scenario is this technique most appropriately applied?
A) Prioritizing VoIP traffic over other traffic types
B) Limiting peer-to-peer file sharing traffic to prevent it from consuming all available WAN bandwidth
C) Guaranteeing minimum bandwidth for video conferencing
D) Preventing routing loops in OSPF
Correct: B
Explanation: Bandwidth throttling caps the maximum rate at which specific traffic (such as P2P file sharing) can consume bandwidth, ensuring other applications have access to network resources. Prioritizing VoIP and guaranteeing minimum bandwidth for video are achieved through QoS queuing mechanisms, not throttling. Throttling is a punitive technique applied to greedy or low-priority traffic classes, while prioritization is a preferential technique applied to high-priority traffic.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A distance-vector routing protocol is susceptible to routing loops. Which mechanism counts to a maximum hop value (15) to prevent packets from circulating indefinitely, and is a feature of RIP?
A) Split horizon
B) Maximum hop count
C) Route poisoning
D) Hold-down timer
Correct: B
Explanation: RIP uses a maximum hop count of 15 as infinity; any route with a hop count of 16 is considered unreachable, preventing packets from circulating through a routing loop indefinitely. Split horizon prevents a router from advertising a route back out the interface through which it was learned, which is a different loop prevention mechanism. RIP's 15-hop maximum effectively limits its deployment to small networks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Which OSPF network type is used on a point-to-point serial link between two routers and does not require a Designated Router (DR) election?
A) Broadcast multi-access
B) Non-broadcast multi-access (NBMA)
C) Point-to-point
D) Point-to-multipoint
Correct: C
Explanation: OSPF point-to-point network type is used on links connecting exactly two routers and skips the DR/BDR election process since there is no need to reduce LSA flooding on a link with only two devices. Broadcast multi-access networks (such as Ethernet) require a DR/BDR election to manage the number of adjacencies. Point-to-point is the default OSPF network type on serial interfaces and simplifies configuration on WAN links.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A routing table shows the following entry: O 172.16.0.0/16 [110/20] via 10.0.0.1. What does the value "20" represent?
A) Administrative distance
B) OSPF metric (cost)
C) Hop count
D) Bandwidth in Mbps
Correct: B
Explanation: In the routing table notation [AD/metric], the first number (110) is OSPF's administrative distance and the second number (20) is the OSPF metric (cost), calculated based on reference bandwidth divided by interface bandwidth. The hop count is used as the metric for RIP, not OSPF. OSPF cost is calculated as 100,000,000 / interface bandwidth in bps by default, so a Fast Ethernet interface has a cost of 1 and a T1 has a cost of approximately 64.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: Which type of routing protocol sends its full routing table to neighbours at regular intervals and is susceptible to slow convergence?
A) Link-state
B) Path-vector
C) Distance-vector
D) Hybrid
Correct: C
Explanation: Distance-vector protocols (such as RIP) periodically send their complete routing table to directly connected neighbours, leading to slow convergence because changes must propagate hop by hop across the network. Link-state protocols flood topology information immediately upon a change and converge much faster. Distance-vector protocols are described by the phrase "routing by rumour" because each router only knows what its neighbours have told it, without a complete topology view.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network administrator wants to logically separate departmental traffic on a single physical switch without additional hardware. Which feature should be configured?
A) STP
B) Port security
C) VLANs
D) LACP
Correct: C
Explanation: VLANs (Virtual Local Area Networks) create logical broadcast domain separation on a single physical switch by assigning ports to different VLANs, isolating traffic between departments without requiring separate physical switches. STP (Spanning Tree Protocol) prevents Layer 2 loops but does not separate traffic. VLANs are fundamental to modern network design because they improve security, reduce broadcast domains, and simplify network management.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A switch port connecting to another switch needs to carry traffic for multiple VLANs simultaneously. Which port type and standard should be used?
A) Access port using 802.1D
B) Trunk port using 802.1Q
C) Voice VLAN port using 802.1p
D) Mirror port using SPAN
Correct: B
Explanation: An 802.1Q trunk port tags Ethernet frames with a VLAN ID so that multiple VLANs can be carried across a single inter-switch link, allowing both switches to differentiate frames belonging to different VLANs. An access port carries traffic for only a single VLAN and does not add a VLAN tag. 802.1Q trunking is the IEEE standard for VLAN tagging and is universally supported across multi-vendor switch environments.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: What is the native VLAN on an 802.1Q trunk, and what is its significance?
A) The VLAN used for management traffic; it cannot be changed
B) The VLAN whose frames are sent untagged across the trunk; it must match on both ends
C) The VLAN with the highest priority; it is always VLAN 1
D) A reserved VLAN that carries STP BPDUs only
Correct: B
Explanation: The native VLAN is the one VLAN on an 802.1Q trunk whose frames are transmitted without a VLAN tag; both sides of the trunk must agree on the same native VLAN or a VLAN mismatch will cause connectivity issues. Management traffic does not have to use the native VLAN; it is a security best practice to change the native VLAN away from VLAN 1. VLAN mismatch on the native VLAN is a common troubleshooting scenario because frames arrive on the wrong VLAN silently.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Spanning Tree Protocol (IEEE 802.1D) was designed to solve which Layer 2 problem?
A) VLAN segmentation
B) Broadcast storms caused by Layer 2 loops
C) MAC address table overflow
D) Trunk port negotiation
Correct: B
Explanation: STP prevents broadcast storms by detecting and blocking redundant paths in the Layer 2 network, ensuring there is only one active path between any two network segments while keeping backup paths available. MAC address table overflow is a different attack (MAC flooding) that STP does not address. STP is essential in any network with redundant switch connections; without it, a single broadcast frame would circulate indefinitely, consuming all available bandwidth.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Which STP variant defined by IEEE 802.1w significantly reduces convergence time compared to 802.1D by allowing ports to transition directly to forwarding from discarding?
A) MSTP (802.1s)
B) PVST+
C) RSTP (802.1w)
D) STP (802.1D)
Correct: C
Explanation: RSTP (Rapid Spanning Tree Protocol, 802.1w) reduces convergence from the 30-50 second convergence time of 802.1D to sub-second convergence by introducing new port roles (Alternate and Backup) and a proposal/agreement handshake mechanism. MSTP (802.1s) builds on RSTP but maps multiple VLANs to a single spanning tree instance. RSTP's rapid convergence is achieved through active topology negotiation rather than relying solely on timers.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Multiple Spanning Tree Protocol (MSTP, 802.1s) improves upon RSTP by providing which additional capability?
A) Sub-second failover for a single spanning tree instance
B) Mapping multiple VLANs to multiple spanning tree instances for load balancing
C) Automatic trunk negotiation between switches
D) PoE power budgeting across multiple switches
Correct: B
Explanation: MSTP groups VLANs into spanning tree instances (MSTIs), allowing different VLANs to use different forwarding paths, which enables load balancing across redundant links. RSTP provides fast convergence but still runs a single spanning tree for all VLANs, wasting redundant links. MSTP combines RSTP's rapid convergence with the ability to distribute traffic across multiple paths, making it the most scalable and efficient STP variant.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A switch port is configured with port security to allow a maximum of two MAC addresses and to shut down if a violation occurs. An attacker connects a hub with three devices to this port. What will happen?
A) All three devices will be allowed because hubs do not have MAC addresses
B) The port will enter err-disable state after detecting a violation
C) The switch will block only the third device and allow the first two
D) Port security will be disabled automatically
Correct: B
Explanation: When a port security violation occurs (more unique source MACs than the configured maximum), the default violation mode "shutdown" places the port into err-disable state, effectively disabling the port until an administrator manually re-enables it. The switch counts individual MAC addresses from devices behind the hub; since hubs forward frames from all connected devices, each device's MAC is seen on the switch port. Err-disable provides a strong deterrent against unauthorized device connections.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network administrator needs to capture all traffic passing through a switch port connected to a server for security analysis. The packet capture device is connected to a different port on the same switch. Which feature should be configured?
A) Port security
B) LACP
C) SPAN (port mirroring)
D) Flow control
Correct: C
Explanation: SPAN (Switched Port Analyzer), also called port mirroring, copies all frames sent or received on a source port to a designated destination port where a packet capture device or IDS is connected. LACP bundles multiple physical links into a logical channel and is unrelated to traffic monitoring. SPAN allows non-intrusive traffic monitoring without interrupting production traffic, making it essential for security analysis and troubleshooting.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A VoIP phone is connected to a switch port that also provides data connectivity to a PC. Which VLAN feature separates voice traffic from data traffic on the same physical port?
A) Native VLAN
B) Voice VLAN
C) Management VLAN
D) Private VLAN
Correct: B
Explanation: A voice VLAN (also called auxiliary VLAN) is configured on a switch access port to carry tagged VoIP traffic from the IP phone on a dedicated VLAN while the PC's data traffic remains on the untagged access VLAN. The native VLAN carries untagged traffic and is not specific to voice; using it for voice would not provide separation. The voice VLAN allows QoS policies to be applied specifically to voice traffic, ensuring proper prioritisation for time-sensitive call data.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Which IEEE standard defines Power over Ethernet (PoE) that delivers up to 15.4 watts per port to power devices such as IP phones and basic wireless access points?
A) 802.3bt
B) 802.3at
C) 802.3af
D) 802.3ad
Correct: C
Explanation: IEEE 802.3af (PoE) delivers up to 15.4 watts at the switch port (12.95 W at the powered device) and is sufficient for IP phones, basic cameras, and access points. 802.3at (PoE+) doubles the power to 30 watts per port, while 802.3bt (PoE++) supports up to 60 or 90 watts. Knowing the PoE standard determines which devices can be powered; high-power devices like PTZ cameras or newer 802.11ax APs typically require PoE+ or PoE++.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network engineer bundles four Gigabit Ethernet links between two switches into a single logical 4 Gbps link using an IEEE open standard. Which protocol is being used?
A) LACP (802.3ad)
B) PAgP
C) RSTP (802.1w)
D) CDP
Correct: A
Explanation: LACP (Link Aggregation Control Protocol), defined in IEEE 802.3ad (now 802.1AX), is the open standard protocol for negotiating and managing link aggregation (EtherChannel/port-channel) between switches. PAgP (Port Aggregation Protocol) is Cisco proprietary and performs a similar function but is not interoperable with non-Cisco equipment. LACP provides load balancing and redundancy; if one physical link fails, traffic is redistributed across the remaining links without interruption.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Which Cisco proprietary Layer 2 protocol discovers directly connected Cisco devices and provides information such as device type, IP address, and interface details?
A) LLDP
B) STP
C) CDP
D) LACP
Correct: C
Explanation: CDP (Cisco Discovery Protocol) is a Cisco proprietary Layer 2 protocol that runs on Cisco devices and periodically advertises device information to directly connected neighbours, including device type, IOS version, IP address, and interface details. LLDP (Link Layer Discovery Protocol) is the IEEE open standard equivalent (802.1AB) that performs the same function across multi-vendor environments. CDP is enabled by default on Cisco devices and is invaluable for network documentation, but should be disabled on untrusted interfaces for security.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network administrator wants a vendor-neutral neighbour discovery protocol that works across switches and routers from multiple manufacturers. Which protocol should be used?
A) CDP
B) STP
C) LLDP
D) RSTP
Correct: C
Explanation: LLDP (Link Layer Discovery Protocol, IEEE 802.1AB) is the vendor-neutral standard for Layer 2 neighbour discovery, supported by virtually all modern network equipment regardless of manufacturer. CDP is Cisco proprietary and only exchanges information between Cisco devices. LLDP is essential in multi-vendor environments and is also used by LLDP-MED extensions to communicate PoE and voice VLAN information to IP phones.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Jumbo frames on an Ethernet network refer to frames with an MTU larger than the standard 1500 bytes. What is the most common jumbo frame MTU used in storage and data centre networks?
A) 4096 bytes
B) 9000 bytes
C) 1518 bytes
D) 65535 bytes
Correct: B
Explanation: The most common jumbo frame size used in data centre and storage networks (such as iSCSI SANs) is 9000 bytes MTU, which reduces CPU overhead by requiring fewer frames to transmit large amounts of data. 1518 bytes is the standard Ethernet maximum frame size (including the 802.1Q tag), not a jumbo frame. Jumbo frames must be enabled end-to-end on all switches, routers, and NICs in the path, or fragmentation will occur.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Flow control in Ethernet uses which mechanism to signal an overwhelmed device to temporarily pause frame transmission from the sending device?
A) STP BPDU
B) PAUSE frames (802.3x)
C) LACP PDUs
D) CDP advertisements
Correct: B
Explanation: IEEE 802.3x flow control uses PAUSE frames, which a receiving device sends when its buffers are filling, instructing the transmitting device to stop sending for a specified duration. STP BPDUs are used for loop prevention, not flow control. Flow control is particularly important in storage networks and high-speed links where buffer overflow would cause packet drops and TCP retransmissions.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A switch administrator needs to prevent unauthorized devices from connecting to specific switch ports by only allowing specific MAC addresses to communicate. Which feature accomplishes this?
A) 802.1Q trunking
B) MAC filtering / port security
C) SPAN
D) VLAN tagging
Correct: B
Explanation: MAC filtering (implemented through port security) restricts which MAC addresses are permitted to send frames through a switch port, blocking unauthorized devices from communicating. 802.1Q trunking tags frames with VLAN IDs for inter-switch transport and does not restrict device access. Port security can be configured with static MAC addresses or sticky learning, which dynamically learns and locks the first MAC addresses seen on a port.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: An administrator configures PoE+ on a switch to power a PTZ security camera requiring 25 watts. Which IEEE standard supports this power level?
A) 802.3af
B) 802.3at
C) 802.3ab
D) 802.3bt
Correct: B
Explanation: IEEE 802.3at (PoE+) delivers up to 30 watts at the switch port (25.5 W at the powered device), making it suitable for PTZ cameras, dual-radio access points, and other higher-power devices. 802.3af delivers a maximum of 15.4 watts, which is insufficient for 25-watt devices. 802.3bt (PoE++) delivers up to 60-90 watts and would be used for even higher-power devices such as video conferencing endpoints.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network engineer troubleshooting a loop in the network notices that one switch port is in the BLK (blocking) state in STP. What does this mean?
A) The port has been administratively shut down
B) The port is receiving BPDUs and is preventing a forwarding loop by not forwarding data frames
C) The port has failed due to a hardware error
D) The port is in err-disable state due to a security violation
Correct: B
Explanation: A port in STP blocking state receives and processes BPDUs to maintain topology awareness but does not forward data frames, preventing a Layer 2 loop. An administratively shut-down port is in the down/down state, not a STP blocking state. Blocking ports are part of normal STP operation; they represent redundant paths that will transition to forwarding if the active path fails.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: RSPAN extends port mirroring to allow traffic captured on one switch to be monitored on a port located on a different switch. How does RSPAN differ from local SPAN?
A) RSPAN uses CDP to forward captured frames, while SPAN uses STP
B) RSPAN carries mirrored traffic across the network using a dedicated RSPAN VLAN over trunk links
C) RSPAN requires PoE-enabled ports, while SPAN does not
D) RSPAN only captures ingress traffic, while SPAN captures both ingress and egress
Correct: B
Explanation: RSPAN (Remote SPAN) encapsulates mirrored traffic in a dedicated RSPAN VLAN and forwards it across trunk links to a destination port on a remote switch, enabling centralized network monitoring across a multi-switch environment. Standard SPAN only works within a single switch. RSPAN is essential in large campus networks where security monitoring equipment cannot be co-located with every switch.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Which IEEE 802.11 standard operates exclusively in the 5 GHz band, provides a maximum theoretical throughput of 54 Mbps, and was designed to avoid 2.4 GHz interference?
A) 802.11b
B) 802.11g
C) 802.11a
D) 802.11n
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11a operates exclusively in the 5 GHz band at up to 54 Mbps using OFDM modulation, making it immune to the interference that plagued 2.4 GHz 802.11b deployments. 802.11g operates in the 2.4 GHz band at up to 54 Mbps and is backward compatible with 802.11b. The 5 GHz band used by 802.11a provides more non-overlapping channels than 2.4 GHz but offers less range due to higher frequency signal attenuation.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Which 802.11 standard introduced MIMO (Multiple Input Multiple Output) antenna technology and was the first to operate in both the 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz bands?
A) 802.11a
B) 802.11g
C) 802.11n
D) 802.11ac
Correct: C
Explanation: 802.11n (Wi-Fi 4) introduced MIMO with up to four spatial streams and channel bonding (40 MHz channels), and was the first dual-band standard supporting both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz operation, with maximum theoretical throughput of 600 Mbps. 802.11ac operates exclusively in the 5 GHz band and introduced MU-MIMO. 802.11n's dual-band capability allowed organizations to deploy both bands simultaneously to improve client density and reduce interference.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
