Question: A wireless engineer is deploying 802.11ac access points. In which frequency band do these APs operate?
A) 2.4 GHz only
B) 5 GHz only
C) Both 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz
D) 6 GHz only
Correct: B
Explanation: 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5) operates exclusively in the 5 GHz band, leveraging wider channels (up to 160 MHz), up to eight spatial streams, and MU-MIMO to achieve theoretical speeds up to 6.9 Gbps. 802.11n was the previous dual-band standard; 802.11ac dropped 2.4 GHz support. The 5 GHz band provides more non-overlapping channels and less congestion than 2.4 GHz, but has shorter range, which is mitigated by deploying more APs at closer spacing.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: 802.11ax (Wi-Fi 6) introduces OFDMA to improve performance in dense environments. What does OFDMA enable that 802.11ac's OFDM does not?
A) Wider channel bonding up to 320 MHz
B) Operation in the 6 GHz band
C) Simultaneous transmission to multiple clients within a single channel using sub-carriers
D) Use of the 2.4 GHz band for backhaul
Correct: C
Explanation: OFDMA (Orthogonal Frequency Division Multiple Access) divides a channel into smaller resource units (sub-carriers) allowing an AP to transmit to multiple clients simultaneously within the same channel, improving efficiency in dense environments. OFDM (used in 802.11ac) transmits to only one client at a time per channel. Wi-Fi 6E adds 6 GHz band support, and Wi-Fi 6E/7 introduce 320 MHz channels; 802.11ax itself primarily adds 2.4 and 5 GHz improvements plus OFDMA.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Wi-Fi 6E extends the 802.11ax standard by adding which frequency band that significantly reduces interference?
A) 900 MHz
B) 2.4 GHz
C) 5 GHz
D) 6 GHz
Correct: D
Explanation: Wi-Fi 6E extends Wi-Fi 6 (802.11ax) to the newly available 6 GHz band, which provides up to 1,200 MHz of additional spectrum and 59 new 20 MHz channels that are free from legacy device interference. 2.4 GHz and 5 GHz are already congested with older Wi-Fi generations and non-Wi-Fi devices. The 6 GHz band is a greenfield deployment space where only Wi-Fi 6E and newer devices can connect, ensuring optimal performance.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: In the 2.4 GHz band, how many non-overlapping 20 MHz channels are available in North America?
A) 1
B) 3
C) 11
D) 23
Correct: B
Explanation: The 2.4 GHz band has 11 channels available in North America, but due to channel overlap (each 20 MHz channel overlaps adjacent channels), only channels 1, 6, and 11 are non-overlapping. Deploying APs on the same channel causes co-channel interference, which is worse than adjacent channel interference. The limited number of non-overlapping channels is a major limitation of the 2.4 GHz band, making the 5 GHz band (with up to 25 non-overlapping 20 MHz channels) preferable for high-density deployments.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Channel bonding in 802.11n combines two 20 MHz channels into a 40 MHz channel. What is the primary trade-off of using 40 MHz channels in the 2.4 GHz band?
A) Reduced data rates compared to 20 MHz channels
B) Significantly fewer non-overlapping channels, causing increased interference
C) Incompatibility with 802.11a devices
D) Inability to use WPA2 security
Correct: B
Explanation: In the 2.4 GHz band, using 40 MHz channels leaves only one non-overlapping channel (instead of three), which causes severe co-channel interference in any environment with neighbouring APs or networks. In the 5 GHz band, 40 MHz channels are much more practical due to the greater number of available channels. 802.11n channel bonding is generally recommended only in the 5 GHz band for high-density deployments; 20 MHz channels are preferred in the 2.4 GHz band.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: WPA3 improves upon WPA2 personal mode by implementing which key security enhancement that protects against offline dictionary attacks?
A) RC4 encryption instead of AES
B) Simultaneous Authentication of Equals (SAE)
C) TKIP key mixing
D) Pre-Shared Key (PSK) with longer passwords
Correct: B
Explanation: WPA3-Personal uses SAE (Simultaneous Authentication of Equals, based on the Dragonfly handshake) instead of WPA2's PSK mechanism, providing forward secrecy and protection against offline dictionary attacks even if the passphrase is captured. WPA2's PSK exchange can be captured and subjected to offline brute-force attacks; SAE prevents this because the key derivation cannot be performed without completing the online exchange. WPA3's SAE also protects against KRACK-style key reinstallation attacks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: An enterprise wireless network requires users to authenticate individually using their Active Directory credentials rather than a shared passphrase. Which combination of technologies is most appropriate?
A) WPA2-Personal with a complex PSK
B) WPA2-Enterprise with RADIUS and 802.1X
C) WPA3-Personal with SAE
D) Open authentication with a captive portal
Correct: B
Explanation: WPA2-Enterprise combined with 802.1X and a RADIUS server allows individual user authentication using credentials (username/password or certificates), providing per-user accountability and centralized access control. WPA2-Personal uses a shared passphrase that all users know, making it impossible to revoke access for individual users without changing the passphrase for everyone. WPA2/WPA3-Enterprise with RADIUS is the standard for corporate wireless networks because it integrates with existing directory services and supports certificate-based authentication.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Which EAP type uses client and server certificates for mutual authentication, providing the strongest form of wireless authentication?
A) PEAP
B) EAP-MD5
C) EAP-TLS
D) LEAP
Correct: C
Explanation: EAP-TLS (EAP Transport Layer Security) requires both the client and the RADIUS server to present digital certificates, providing mutual authentication and the strongest security among common EAP types. PEAP (Protected EAP) only requires a server-side certificate and uses a tunnelled inner method (typically MSCHAPv2) for client authentication. EAP-TLS's reliance on client certificates makes it the most secure EAP type but also the most operationally complex due to certificate lifecycle management.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: PEAP encapsulates an inner authentication method within a TLS tunnel. What is the primary advantage of PEAP over EAP-TLS in terms of infrastructure requirements?
A) PEAP provides faster authentication because it uses fewer round trips
B) PEAP only requires a server-side certificate, eliminating the need to deploy client certificates
C) PEAP supports more cipher suites than EAP-TLS
D) PEAP operates without a RADIUS server
Correct: B
Explanation: PEAP creates a TLS tunnel using only a server certificate and then authenticates the client within that tunnel using credentials (typically MSCHAPv2), eliminating the need to issue and manage certificates on every client device. EAP-TLS requires client certificates on every device, which is operationally challenging in large environments without a mature PKI. PEAP is the most widely deployed enterprise EAP type because it balances strong security with simpler client provisioning.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless engineer needs to provide wide coverage in a large open warehouse using a single access point. Which antenna type provides equal signal radiation in all horizontal directions?
A) Directional
B) Yagi
C) Patch
D) Omnidirectional
Correct: D
Explanation: An omnidirectional antenna radiates signal equally in all horizontal directions (360 degrees), making it ideal for covering open areas from a centrally located access point. A Yagi antenna is highly directional with a narrow beam width, making it suitable for point-to-point links or covering a long narrow area. Omnidirectional antennas are the most common type used in indoor enterprise APs because they provide symmetric coverage without requiring precise alignment.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless engineer needs to establish a long-distance point-to-point wireless link between two buildings 2 km apart. Which antenna type is most appropriate?
A) Omnidirectional
B) Patch
C) Yagi
D) Dipole
Correct: C
Explanation: A Yagi antenna is a highly directional antenna with high gain and a narrow beam width, making it ideal for long-distance point-to-point wireless links where signal must be focused in a single direction to maximize range. Omnidirectional antennas waste signal in unwanted directions, reducing effective range and gain. Yagi antennas require precise alignment between the two endpoints but deliver significantly better link budgets than omnidirectional antennas for outdoor point-to-point connections.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: During a wireless site survey, a network engineer uses heat maps to analyse which aspect of the wireless deployment?
A) IP address allocation for wireless clients
B) Signal strength and coverage across the physical space
C) Authentication server availability
D) DHCP lease times for wireless devices
Correct: B
Explanation: Heat maps display the spatial distribution of signal strength (RSSI) across a floor plan or physical area, allowing engineers to identify coverage gaps, dead zones, and areas of excessive overlap. IP address allocation and DHCP are not assessed through heat maps. Heat maps are a critical output of wireless site surveys and are used during both pre-deployment planning (predictive surveys) and post-deployment validation (passive surveys) to ensure adequate coverage.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Which wireless deployment model uses a centralized controller to manage configuration, roaming, and RF policies for all access points in the network?
A) Autonomous AP
B) Cloud-managed AP with local switching
C) Controller-based (thin AP) architecture
D) Fat AP standalone deployment
Correct: C
Explanation: Controller-based (thin AP) architecture centralizes management, roaming decisions, and RF policies on a Wireless LAN Controller (WLC), with APs (thin/lightweight APs) acting as radio frequency front-ends that tunnel client traffic to the controller. Autonomous (fat) APs manage their own configuration independently and are more complex to manage at scale. Controller-based architecture simplifies large-scale deployments, enables seamless roaming between APs, and allows centralized policy enforcement.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Band steering is a wireless feature that encourages compatible clients to connect to which frequency band to improve overall network performance?
A) 2.4 GHz, because it has longer range
B) 5 GHz, because it offers more channels and higher throughput
C) 6 GHz, because it is mandatory for Wi-Fi 6 clients
D) 900 MHz, because it has better wall penetration
Correct: B
Explanation: Band steering detects dual-band capable clients and steers them toward the 5 GHz band, which offers more non-overlapping channels, higher maximum throughput, and less congestion than the 2.4 GHz band. The 2.4 GHz band is reserved by band steering for legacy single-band clients and devices that need greater range. By offloading capable clients to 5 GHz, band steering reduces interference in the 2.4 GHz band and improves the experience for all clients.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: MU-MIMO (Multi-User MIMO) was introduced in which Wi-Fi standard and allows an AP to transmit to multiple clients simultaneously?
A) 802.11n (Wi-Fi 4) — downlink MU-MIMO
B) 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5) — downlink MU-MIMO
C) 802.11g — bidirectional MU-MIMO
D) 802.11a — uplink MU-MIMO
Correct: B
Explanation: 802.11ac (Wi-Fi 5) Wave 2 introduced downlink MU-MIMO, allowing the AP to transmit to up to four clients simultaneously using spatial multiplexing. 802.11n introduced MIMO but only for single-user (SU-MIMO) operation, where only one client could be served at a time. 802.11ax (Wi-Fi 6) extended MU-MIMO to support both uplink and downlink simultaneously for up to eight clients.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless engineer is performing a pre-deployment site survey. A predictive survey uses which approach to plan AP placement before installation?
A) Walking the physical space with an AP and laptop to measure actual signal strength
B) Using software to model RF propagation based on floor plan dimensions and construction materials
C) Reviewing existing DHCP logs to identify wireless client density
D) Interviewing users about their current wireless experience
Correct: B
Explanation: A predictive (passive) site survey uses RF planning software to model signal propagation based on floor plan geometry, wall materials, and AP specifications without physically deploying equipment. A passive survey walking the space with an AP measures actual RF conditions and is called an active or passive on-site survey. Predictive surveys accelerate deployment planning by identifying optimal AP placement and count before any hardware is purchased or installed.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless client roams from AP1 to AP2 in a controller-based WLAN. What mechanism ensures the client session is maintained without re-authentication?
A) 802.1Q trunking between APs
B) RSTP topology recalculation
C) Fast BSS Transition (802.11r) or controller-managed roaming
D) WPA3-SAE re-keying
Correct: C
Explanation: In a controller-based architecture, the WLC manages client state and can hand off sessions between APs without requiring the client to re-authenticate to the RADIUS server; 802.11r (Fast BSS Transition) further reduces roaming latency by pre-authenticating with candidate APs. 802.1Q trunking is for wired VLAN transport between switches, not wireless roaming. Seamless roaming is critical for real-time applications like VoIP, where even a brief authentication delay would cause a noticeable gap in call audio.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: An 802.11ax access point in a dense stadium deployment uses OFDMA resource units to schedule uplink transmissions from multiple clients simultaneously. This improves which wireless metric most directly?
A) Maximum single-client throughput
B) Overall spectral efficiency and capacity in high-density environments
C) AP transmit power and range
D) WPA3 authentication speed
Correct: B
Explanation: OFDMA's ability to allocate small resource units to multiple clients simultaneously dramatically improves spectral efficiency in high-density environments by reducing idle channel time and overhead from per-client channel access. Maximum single-client throughput may actually be slightly lower with OFDMA since the full channel is shared, but aggregate network capacity increases significantly. OFDMA is the primary reason Wi-Fi 6 provides better real-world performance in crowded environments like stadiums and conference halls even without increasing raw data rates.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A network technician is troubleshooting a bus topology network and discovers that all devices have lost connectivity simultaneously. What is the most likely cause?
A) A single device has failed
B) The central switch has failed
C) A break or termination fault exists in the shared cable
D) STP has placed all ports in blocking state
Correct: C
Explanation: In a bus topology, all devices share a single cable; a break anywhere in the cable or a failed terminator causes signal reflection or disruption that affects all devices simultaneously. A single device failure in any topology only affects that device, not the entire network. This is the fundamental weakness of bus topology and the reason it has been replaced by star topology, where a single link failure only isolates one device.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A router receives a packet destined for 10.30.5.1. The routing table contains entries for 10.30.0.0/16 and 10.30.5.0/24. Which route will the router use?
A) 10.30.0.0/16, because it was learned first
B) 10.30.5.0/24, because longest prefix match is always preferred
C) Both routes simultaneously for load balancing
D) Neither route; the router will send an ICMP unreachable
Correct: B
Explanation: Routers use longest prefix match (most specific route) when multiple routes match a destination; 10.30.5.0/24 has a longer prefix (24 bits) than 10.30.0.0/16 (16 bits), so it is more specific and selected. Administrative distance and metric are only used when multiple routes from different or same sources have equal prefix length. Longest prefix match is the fundamental routing decision algorithm and is why subnetting allows precise traffic steering.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network administrator discovers that a switch is flooding unknown unicast traffic out all ports in a VLAN, causing excessive traffic. What is the most likely cause?
A) A routing loop in the network
B) The destination MAC address is not in the switch's MAC address table
C) STP has placed the port in forwarding state
D) LACP has failed on the uplink
Correct: B
Explanation: When a switch receives a unicast frame with a destination MAC address not found in its MAC address table, it floods the frame out all ports in the same VLAN except the ingress port, a process called unknown unicast flooding. A routing loop occurs at Layer 3 and would not cause MAC address flooding. MAC table flooding can be a symptom of a MAC flooding attack (which deliberately overflows the table with fake entries, causing the switch to flood all traffic).

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A switch administrator has configured VLAN 10 on switchport Gi0/1 as an access port. A new device is connected to the port and cannot communicate with other VLAN 10 devices on a different switch. Inter-switch link is a trunk. What should the administrator verify first?
A) That VLAN 10 exists in the VLAN database on both switches
B) That PoE is enabled on the port
C) That LACP is configured on the access port
D) That STP is disabled on the trunk
Correct: A
Explanation: A VLAN must exist in the VLAN database on a switch before frames tagged for that VLAN will be forwarded over a trunk; if VLAN 10 is not in the allowed VLAN list or does not exist on the remote switch, traffic will be dropped. PoE and LACP are unrelated to VLAN reachability issues. This is a very common troubleshooting scenario: VLAN creation must be verified on all switches in the path, not just the one where the device is connected.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: An OSPF network has several routers on a broadcast multi-access segment. Which two router roles are elected to reduce the number of OSPF adjacencies on the segment?
A) Active Router and Standby Router
B) Designated Router (DR) and Backup Designated Router (BDR)
C) Root Bridge and Backup Root Bridge
D) ABR and ASBR
Correct: B
Explanation: On broadcast multi-access networks (like Ethernet), OSPF elects a DR and BDR to reduce the number of full adjacencies from n(n-1)/2 to 2(n-1); all other routers form adjacencies only with the DR and BDR. Active and Standby Routers are HSRP/VRRP first-hop redundancy roles, not OSPF roles. The DR election is based on the highest OSPF priority (default 1), with the highest Router ID as a tiebreaker.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A technician notices that clients in a conference room 15 metres from an AP consistently get poor performance during large company meetings. The AP is 802.11n operating at 2.4 GHz. What is the most likely cause?
A) The AP is too close to the clients
B) Co-channel interference and client density on the congested 2.4 GHz band
C) The AP's SSID is hidden
D) EAP-TLS certificates have expired
Correct: B
Explanation: The 2.4 GHz band has only three non-overlapping channels, and dense client environments exhaust available airtime quickly due to CSMA/CA contention and potential co-channel interference from neighbouring APs. A hidden SSID would prevent clients from connecting at all, not cause performance degradation during meetings. The solution would be to add a 5 GHz AP for the conference room, use band steering to push clients to 5 GHz, and reduce AP density on 2.4 GHz.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: Which of the following best describes the difference between a LAN and a WAN from a geographic and ownership perspective?
A) A LAN is always wireless; a WAN always uses fibre optic
B) A LAN is typically owned and operated by a single organization within a limited area; a WAN spans large distances and often uses service provider infrastructure
C) A WAN always has higher bandwidth than a LAN
D) A LAN requires a router; a WAN does not
Correct: B
Explanation: A LAN is confined to a building or campus and is typically owned and managed by a single organization, while a WAN connects geographically dispersed locations often using leased lines, MPLS, or internet connections provided by carriers. WANs typically have lower bandwidth at higher cost compared to LANs, not higher bandwidth. This distinction is fundamental to network design because WAN links are usually the bandwidth bottleneck and reliability concern in enterprise networks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A network uses QoS to guarantee a minimum bandwidth of 256 kbps for VoIP traffic during congestion. Which QoS mechanism provides a minimum bandwidth guarantee?
A) Traffic policing
B) Traffic shaping
C) Low Latency Queuing (LLQ) with bandwidth command
D) Best-effort forwarding
Correct: C
Explanation: LLQ (Low Latency Queuing) with a bandwidth guarantee allocates a minimum reserved bandwidth to a class of traffic and provides absolute priority queuing for time-sensitive traffic like VoIP, ensuring it receives its bandwidth even during congestion. Traffic policing drops or re-marks traffic exceeding a rate limit but does not guarantee bandwidth. LLQ combines a strict priority queue for real-time traffic with class-based weighted fair queuing (CBWFQ) for other traffic classes.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: An administrator wants to see all CDP neighbours on a Cisco switch, including their IP addresses and interface connections. Which command would provide this information?
A) show ip route
B) show vlan brief
C) show cdp neighbors detail
D) show spanning-tree
Correct: C
Explanation: The "show cdp neighbors detail" command displays comprehensive information about directly connected Cisco devices, including their hostname, IP address, platform type, IOS version, and the local and remote interfaces. "show ip route" displays the routing table and provides no CDP information. CDP neighbor details are essential for network discovery and documentation, particularly when physical documentation is incomplete.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless deployment uses autonomous access points. How does managing these APs differ from a controller-based deployment?
A) Autonomous APs are centrally managed from a single pane of glass
B) Each autonomous AP must be configured individually, and roaming requires re-authentication
C) Autonomous APs cannot support WPA2 Enterprise
D) Autonomous APs automatically synchronize configurations via CAPWAP
Correct: B
Explanation: Autonomous (fat) APs are standalone devices that each require individual configuration; they do not have a centralized controller for policy distribution, and client roaming between APs typically requires re-authentication because there is no shared state. Controller-based APs use CAPWAP tunnels to a WLC for centralized management and seamless roaming. Autonomous APs are appropriate for small deployments with few APs, but become impractical and difficult to manage at enterprise scale.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A BGP router receives multiple paths to the same prefix from different peers. BGP selects the best path based on a defined attribute order. Which attribute is checked first in the standard BGP best path selection process?
A) Local preference
B) Weight (Cisco proprietary)
C) AS_PATH length
D) MED (Multi-Exit Discriminator)
Correct: B
Explanation: Cisco's BGP best path selection process begins with Weight (highest preferred), which is a Cisco-proprietary attribute that is locally significant to a single router. Local preference is checked second (higher is preferred) and is propagated within an AS. Knowing the BGP best path selection order is critical for Network+ candidates because it explains how traffic engineering policies are implemented in BGP-based enterprise and ISP networks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A Layer 2 switch receives a frame with a destination MAC address of FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF. How does the switch handle this frame?
A) Drops the frame because broadcast addresses are not supported
B) Forwards the frame to the default gateway only
C) Floods the frame out all ports in the same VLAN except the ingress port
D) Forwards the frame only to the device that sent it
Correct: C
Explanation: Broadcast frames (destination MAC FF:FF:FF:FF:FF:FF) are flooded out all ports in the same VLAN except the ingress port; this is fundamental Layer 2 switching behaviour for broadcasts. Switches do not filter or drop broadcasts at Layer 2 (only routers segment broadcast domains). This is why VLANs are essential: without VLANs, broadcast traffic from all devices floods the entire switched network, consuming bandwidth on every device.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A company connects its headquarters to a cloud provider using a dedicated private connection rather than the public internet. Which architecture type does this represent?
A) Peer-to-peer
B) Direct Connect / private WAN cloud connectivity
C) Site-to-site VPN over the internet
D) Autonomous AP deployment
Correct: B
Explanation: Direct Connect (AWS) or ExpressRoute (Azure) provides a dedicated private circuit from the customer's premises to the cloud provider's network, bypassing the public internet and providing consistent bandwidth, lower latency, and enhanced security. A site-to-site VPN uses the public internet as the transport medium and is subject to internet congestion and variable performance. Private cloud connectivity is preferred for organizations with latency-sensitive applications or large data volumes that cannot tolerate internet variability.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A network engineer configures OSPF and notices that two routers are stuck in EXSTART state. What is the most likely cause?
A) Mismatched VLAN configurations
B) MTU mismatch between the two routers' interfaces
C) Incorrect DSCP markings on OSPF packets
D) LACP negotiation failure on the link
Correct: B
Explanation: OSPF routers get stuck in EXSTART/EXCHANGE state when there is an MTU mismatch on the connected interfaces; one router's Database Description packets may be larger than the other can accept, preventing the database exchange from completing. VLAN mismatches would prevent Layer 2 connectivity entirely, so OSPF would not even begin the adjacency process. MTU mismatch is a common OSPF troubleshooting scenario, and the fix is to either match the MTU on both interfaces or use the "ip ospf mtu-ignore" command.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless client is configured with a static IP address but cannot access the network after connecting to the SSID. Other DHCP clients on the same SSID connect successfully. What is the most likely cause?
A) WPA3 is not supported by the client
B) The static IP address is in a different subnet than the wireless VLAN's gateway
C) The RADIUS server has rejected the client
D) Band steering has moved the client to an incompatible channel
Correct: B
Explanation: If a static IP address is configured with an incorrect subnet mask or in a wrong subnet, the client will be unable to reach the default gateway or other devices on the VLAN, even though the wireless association succeeds. DHCP clients succeed because they receive correct addressing automatically from the DHCP server. This is a common Layer 3 troubleshooting scenario: wireless association (Layer 2) can succeed while Layer 3 connectivity fails due to misconfigured static addressing.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: Which STP port role represents the best path back toward the root bridge on a non-root switch?
A) Designated port
B) Alternate port
C) Root port
D) Backup port
Correct: C
Explanation: The root port is the port on a non-root switch with the lowest-cost path to the root bridge; every non-root switch has exactly one root port, and it is always in the forwarding state. A designated port is the forwarding port on each network segment that sends traffic toward the root bridge. Understanding root port selection is essential for predicting traffic paths and planning STP optimization in redundant switch networks.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A branch office router loses its connection to the OSPF network. The floating static default route with AD 200 becomes active. After OSPF reconverges, what happens to the floating static route?
A) It remains active alongside the OSPF routes
B) It is removed from the routing table because the OSPF route (AD 110) is more preferred
C) It becomes the primary route because static routes are always preferred
D) It is converted to an OSPF route automatically
Correct: B
Explanation: When OSPF reconverges and re-installs the dynamic route with AD 110, the floating static route (AD 200) is removed from the active routing table because routers install only the route with the lowest AD for each prefix. The floating static route remains in the configuration but is not used as long as the preferred dynamic route is present. This is the intended behaviour: floating static routes provide automatic failover without manual intervention.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: An 802.11b device connects to an access point that also serves 802.11g clients. What performance impact does the legacy 802.11b client have on the 802.11g clients?
A) No impact; 802.11g clients maintain full throughput regardless
B) The AP switches to 802.11g-only mode and drops the 802.11b client
C) The 802.11b client causes the AP to use lower data rates and longer protection mechanisms, reducing throughput for all clients
D) 802.11g clients cannot associate when an 802.11b client is present
Correct: C
Explanation: When an 802.11b client connects to a mixed 802.11b/g network, the AP must use CTS-to-Self or RTS/CTS protection mechanisms to ensure 802.11b clients receive frames, which adds overhead and reduces the channel efficiency for all clients including 802.11g devices. The AP does not drop the legacy client; it accommodates it at the expense of network performance. This is why modern networks often disable 802.11b data rates (1, 2, 5.5, 11 Mbps) to improve overall network performance.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: A network administrator enables PortFast on a switch access port connected to a server. What does PortFast do?
A) It disables STP entirely on the switch
B) It allows the port to immediately transition to forwarding state, bypassing STP listening and learning states
C) It enables the port to carry multiple VLANs simultaneously
D) It enables PoE on the port immediately upon device connection
Correct: B
Explanation: PortFast allows a port to skip the STP listening (15 sec) and learning (15 sec) states and immediately enter the forwarding state, eliminating the 30-second delay that would otherwise prevent the connected device from communicating immediately upon connection. PortFast should only be enabled on ports connected to end devices, never on ports connected to other switches, because it cannot detect a topology change that would warrant keeping the port in blocking state. PortFast should always be used with BPDU Guard to shut down the port if a switch is accidentally connected.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A network engineer implements QoS DSCP marking and notices that the markings are being reset to default (DSCP 0) at a service provider handoff. What is the most likely reason?
A) The service provider's router does not support DSCP
B) The service provider has a policy to remark or ignore customer DSCP markings at the network edge
C) DSCP markings are stripped when frames traverse a VLAN trunk
D) WPA3 authentication resets DSCP values
Correct: B
Explanation: Many service providers re-mark or ignore customer DSCP values at their network boundary as a policy measure, requiring customers to re-apply QoS markings after the handoff or negotiate a QoS agreement with the provider. DSCP is an IP header field and survives routing and VLAN trunking; it is not stripped at Layer 2 boundaries. End-to-end QoS requires coordination at every network boundary, particularly at service provider handoff points where trust boundaries exist.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: In a client-server network model, which device typically provides centralized authentication, file storage, and print services?
A) End-user workstation
B) Dedicated server
C) Network switch
D) Wireless access point
Correct: B
Explanation: In the client-server model, dedicated servers provide centralized services (authentication via Active Directory, file sharing via SMB, print services via print spooler) that client workstations access over the network. End-user workstations are the clients that request services, not the providers. The client-server model is preferred over peer-to-peer in organizations of any significant size because it centralizes management, improves security, and scales better.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: An administrator wants to prevent unknown devices from connecting by having the switch learn and permanently lock the first MAC address seen on each access port. Which port security feature accomplishes this?
A) Static MAC address entry
B) Sticky MAC address learning
C) MAC filtering with ACL
D) 802.1Q trunking
Correct: B
Explanation: Sticky MAC address learning (also called sticky learning) dynamically learns the first MAC address(es) seen on a port and converts them to secure sticky entries that persist in the running configuration (and optionally the startup config), locking the port to the learned device. Static MAC address entry requires manually specifying each MAC address, which is impractical for large deployments. Sticky learning combines the ease of dynamic learning with the permanence of static entries, making it efficient for locking down access ports at scale.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A wireless client shows a strong RSSI signal but experiences poor throughput. An administrator checks the AP and finds significant retry rates. What is the most likely cause?
A) The client is using a static IP address
B) RF interference is causing high error rates and retransmissions
C) The RADIUS server authentication is timing out
D) LACP has failed on the AP uplink
Correct: B
Explanation: High retry rates despite strong RSSI indicate RF interference causing frame errors rather than signal weakness; the signal is strong enough to connect but corrupted enough to require frequent retransmission, reducing effective throughput. Static IP addressing would not cause retry rates; it would only affect Layer 3 connectivity. RF interference sources such as microwave ovens, cordless phones, and competing Wi-Fi networks are common causes of high retry rates, and can be identified using a wireless spectrum analyzer.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: An administrator needs to verify which routing protocols are running on a Cisco router and view the current routing table. Which two commands would provide this information?
A) show interfaces and show vlan
B) show ip protocols and show ip route
C) show cdp neighbors and show spanning-tree
D) show port-security and show mac address-table
Correct: B
Explanation: "show ip protocols" displays the routing protocols currently configured and running on the router, including their timers, networks, and neighbours; "show ip route" displays the complete routing table with all learned routes. "show cdp neighbors" and "show spanning-tree" are Layer 2 commands used for switch topology, not routing protocol verification. These two commands are the first-line diagnostic tools for verifying routing protocol operation and troubleshooting IP connectivity issues.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: Which wireless security protocol from the WPA3 suite replaces the 4-way handshake with a dragonfly key exchange and provides forward secrecy?
A) WEP
B) TKIP
C) WPA2-PSK
D) WPA3-SAE
Correct: D
Explanation: WPA3-SAE (Simultaneous Authentication of Equals) replaces WPA2's 4-way handshake with the Dragonfly handshake, providing forward secrecy (past sessions cannot be decrypted even if the passphrase is later compromised) and protection against offline dictionary attacks. WEP and TKIP are deprecated and vulnerable to well-known attacks. WPA3-SAE is the current recommended standard for personal Wi-Fi security and is mandatory on Wi-Fi 6 certified devices.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.3 — Configure and deploy common Ethernet switching features
Question: BPDU Guard is a STP feature that should be enabled on which type of switch ports to prevent unauthorized switches from being connected?
A) Trunk ports connecting to other switches
B) Access ports connected to end devices with PortFast enabled
C) Uplink ports to the distribution layer
D) Mirror ports running SPAN
Correct: B
Explanation: BPDU Guard should be enabled on access ports configured with PortFast; if a BPDU (Bridge Protocol Data Unit) is received on such a port (indicating a switch has been connected), the port is immediately placed in err-disable state. Trunk ports connecting to known switches need to receive BPDUs for STP operation and must not have BPDU Guard. BPDU Guard is a critical security and stability feature that prevents users from inadvertently or maliciously connecting rogue switches that could disrupt the STP topology.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.1 — Compare and contrast various network topologies, architectures, and types
Question: A technology allows multiple tenant networks to share the same physical network infrastructure while maintaining complete logical isolation. Which technology provides this capability in a service provider environment?
A) VLAN trunking with 802.1Q
B) MPLS Layer 3 VPN (L3VPN)
C) PPPoE dial-up
D) NFC pairing
Correct: B
Explanation: MPLS L3VPN uses VRF (Virtual Routing and Forwarding) tables and MPLS labels to provide complete routing table separation between multiple customer networks sharing the same provider infrastructure. 802.1Q VLAN trunking provides Layer 2 separation within a single organization's network but does not scale to multi-tenant service provider deployments. MPLS L3VPN is the standard enterprise WAN service offered by carriers, allowing hundreds of customers to share the same physical infrastructure with guaranteed isolation.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.2 — Compare and contrast routing technologies and bandwidth management
Question: A network engineer notices intermittent connectivity loss to a remote site that is connected via OSPF. The OSPF neighbour relationship repeatedly drops and re-establishes. What should be investigated first?
A) VLAN configuration on the access layer switches
B) OSPF hello and dead interval timer mismatches between the two routers
C) PortFast configuration on end-device ports
D) RADIUS server availability
Correct: B
Explanation: OSPF neighbour relationships fail when hello or dead intervals do not match between adjacent routers; if the dead interval expires before a hello is received, the neighbour is declared down and the adjacency resets. VLAN and PortFast configurations do not affect Layer 3 OSPF neighbour relationships. OSPF timers must match on both ends of a link; by default hello=10 seconds and dead=40 seconds on broadcast links, and hello=30 seconds, dead=120 seconds on NBMA links.

Domain: 2.0 Network Implementation
Sub-objective: 2.4 — Install and configure wireless standards and technologies
Question: A patch antenna is commonly used in which deployment scenario?
A) Providing 360-degree horizontal coverage from a ceiling-mounted AP
B) Providing directional coverage on an exterior wall or in a corridor
C) Long-distance point-to-point outdoor bridging between buildings several kilometres apart
D) Creating a personal area network between two smartphones
Correct: B
Explanation: A patch antenna is a flat, low-profile directional antenna with moderate gain and a relatively broad beam width (typically 60-90 degrees), commonly mounted on walls or ceilings to provide directed coverage in corridors, along walls, or in specific zones. A Yagi antenna provides much higher gain and a narrower beam for long-distance point-to-point links. Patch antennas are popular in enterprise indoor deployments where directional coverage is needed without the narrow beam of a Yagi.
Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A network administrator wants to monitor CPU utilization on all routers using a pull-based method where the management station requests data at regular intervals. Which SNMP operation is being described?
A) SNMP Trap
B) SNMP Get
C) SNMP Set
D) SNMP Inform
Correct: B
Explanation: SNMP Get is used by the management station to poll (pull) specific OID values from managed devices at scheduled intervals. SNMP Trap is a push-based mechanism where the device sends unsolicited alerts to the manager when an event occurs. Think of Get as "going to get" data and Trap as the device "setting a trap" to alert you.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: An organization requires encrypted and authenticated SNMP communications between its network management system and managed devices. Which SNMP version should be deployed?
A) SNMPv1
B) SNMPv2c
C) SNMPv3
D) SNMPv2u
Correct: C
Explanation: SNMPv3 is the only version that provides authentication (using MD5 or SHA) and encryption (using DES or AES), making it suitable for secure environments. SNMPv2c improved performance and added 64-bit counters over v1 but still uses community strings in cleartext for authentication. Remember: v3 = security, v2c = community strings, v1 = legacy.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A network device sends an unsolicited message to the SNMP manager alerting it that an interface has gone down. What is this type of message called?
A) SNMP Get-Bulk
B) SNMP Set
C) SNMP Trap
D) SNMP Walk
Correct: C
Explanation: An SNMP Trap is an unsolicited, push-based notification sent from a managed device to the SNMP manager when a specific event or threshold is crossed. SNMP Set is used by the manager to change a value on a managed device, not receive notifications. Traps are like fire alarms — the device initiates the alert without being asked.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: Which data structure on an SNMP-managed device defines the objects that can be monitored and their hierarchical organization?
A) OID
B) MIB
C) Community string
D) Trap receiver
Correct: B
Explanation: A Management Information Base (MIB) is a hierarchical database that defines all manageable objects on a device and their data types, access rights, and descriptions. An OID (Object Identifier) is a specific numeric address used to identify a single object within the MIB hierarchy. Think of MIB as the catalog and OID as the specific item number in that catalog.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A network administrator uses SNMPv2c to monitor devices. The community string "public" is used for read access. What is the primary security risk of this configuration?
A) SNMPv2c does not support SNMP traps
B) The community string is transmitted in cleartext
C) SNMPv2c only supports 32-bit counters
D) The "public" string disables MIB access
Correct: B
Explanation: SNMPv2c community strings are transmitted in cleartext across the network, making them vulnerable to interception with a packet capture tool. SNMPv2c does support traps and introduced 64-bit counters as an improvement over v1. The best mitigation is to use SNMPv3 with authentication and encryption, or at minimum use ACLs to restrict SNMP access.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: An administrator needs to export flow data from a router to a collector to analyze top talkers and bandwidth usage by application. Which technology is best suited for this purpose?
A) SNMP traps
B) Syslog
C) NetFlow
D) RMON
Correct: C
Explanation: NetFlow (Cisco's flow-based telemetry protocol) exports metadata about IP conversations — including source/destination IP, ports, protocols, and byte counts — to a collector for traffic analysis. SNMP traps are event-driven alerts, not traffic flow records. NetFlow gives visibility into who is talking to whom and how much bandwidth each flow consumes.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A vendor-neutral version of NetFlow that is standardized by the IETF and supports variable-length fields is known as which protocol?
A) sFlow
B) RMON
C) IPFIX
D) SNMP v3
Correct: C
Explanation: IPFIX (IP Flow Information Export) is the IETF-standardized evolution of Cisco's NetFlow v9, designed to be vendor-neutral and extensible with variable-length fields. sFlow is a different sampling-based technology that captures packet samples rather than full flow records. IPFIX is the "open standard" flow protocol, while NetFlow is Cisco-proprietary.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: Which flow monitoring technology uses statistical packet sampling at the network device rather than tracking complete flows, making it suitable for very high-speed links?
A) NetFlow
B) IPFIX
C) sFlow
D) SNMP polling
Correct: C
Explanation: sFlow uses statistical sampling — it captures one out of every N packets — which reduces processing overhead and makes it viable on high-speed interfaces where full flow tracking would be impractical. NetFlow and IPFIX track complete flow records which requires more device resources. sFlow trades precision for scalability, providing approximate traffic statistics at wire speed.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A network engineer notices that an interface is showing a high number of CRC errors. What does this most likely indicate?
A) The interface is operating at full duplex when it should be half duplex
B) Physical layer issues such as a faulty cable or connector
C) The SNMP community string is misconfigured
D) The interface MTU is set too high
Correct: B
Explanation: CRC (Cyclic Redundancy Check) errors indicate data corruption during transmission, typically caused by physical layer problems such as damaged cables, faulty connectors, or excessive cable length. Duplex mismatch typically causes late collisions and runts, not CRC errors specifically. CRC errors point to Layer 1 — check physical media first.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A user complains that their VoIP calls have choppy audio even though bandwidth utilization appears normal. Which metric should the administrator investigate?
A) Interface utilization percentage
B) Jitter
C) Broadcast rate
D) MTU size
Correct: B
Explanation: Jitter is the variation in packet delay (inter-packet arrival time) and is the primary cause of choppy VoIP audio even when overall bandwidth is sufficient. High interface utilization would typically cause packet loss rather than jitter. For real-time applications like VoIP and video, consistent low-latency delivery matters more than raw bandwidth.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: Which syslog severity level indicates a condition where the system is unusable?
A) Level 0
B) Level 2
C) Level 4
D) Level 6
Correct: A
Explanation: Syslog severity level 0 is Emergency (emerg), indicating the system is completely unusable — the most critical level. Level 2 is Critical, level 4 is Warning, and level 6 is Informational. Remember the mnemonic "Every Angry Coder Creates Errors, Warnings, Nothing Important" for levels 0-6 (Emergency, Alert, Critical, Error, Warning, Notice, Informational).

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A syslog server is configured to capture messages at severity level 4. Which messages will it collect?
A) Only Warning messages (level 4)
B) Emergency through Warning (levels 0-4)
C) Warning through Debug (levels 4-7)
D) Only Informational and Debug (levels 6-7)
Correct: B
Explanation: Syslog severity levels work as a threshold — when you configure level 4, the system captures that level AND all more severe levels (0 through 4: Emergency, Alert, Critical, Error, Warning). Lower numbers mean higher severity in syslog. This is counterintuitive but important: "level 4 and below" means levels 0, 1, 2, 3, and 4.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: Which syslog severity level is used for normal but significant operational messages, such as a user logging in successfully?
A) Level 3 — Error
B) Level 5 — Notice
C) Level 6 — Informational
D) Level 7 — Debug
Correct: B
Explanation: Level 5 (Notice) is for normal but significant conditions that warrant attention, such as successful logins or configuration changes. Level 6 (Informational) is for routine operational messages like interface status changes. The difference: Notice is "noteworthy normal" while Informational is "routine normal" — both useful but Notice deserves more attention.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: An organization centralizes log collection from all network devices into a single platform that correlates events across multiple sources to identify security incidents. What is this system called?
A) SNMP manager
B) NetFlow collector
C) SIEM
D) Syslog forwarder
Correct: C
Explanation: A SIEM (Security Information and Event Management) system aggregates logs from multiple sources, normalizes them, and applies correlation rules to detect security incidents that might not be apparent from any single log source. An SNMP manager monitors device health metrics, not security event correlation. SIEM = Security Intelligence — it connects the dots across all log sources.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A data center administrator wants to ensure that equipment temperature stays within safe operating ranges and receive alerts when thresholds are exceeded. Which monitoring approach is most appropriate?
A) Configure SNMP traps on temperature sensor OIDs with threshold alerts
B) Use NetFlow to track thermal traffic patterns
C) Enable syslog level 7 on all switches
D) Deploy a packet analyzer near the cooling units
Correct: A
Explanation: Environmental sensors (temperature, humidity) on managed network equipment expose their readings via SNMP OIDs, and SNMP traps can be configured to alert when values exceed safe thresholds. NetFlow tracks IP traffic flows and has no relevance to physical temperature monitoring. Most enterprise switches and servers expose temperature sensor data through their SNMP MIBs.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: An interface on a core switch shows 45% utilization consistently throughout the business day. The administrator wants to establish when this interface needs to be upgraded. What should be configured?
A) A syslog alert at level 3
B) A bandwidth utilization threshold alert at 80%
C) An SNMP trap for CRC errors
D) A NetFlow export to monitor jitter
Correct: B
Explanation: Setting a utilization threshold alert (commonly at 75-80%) provides advance warning before an interface becomes a bottleneck, giving time to plan an upgrade. A syslog level 3 alert is for errors, not capacity planning thresholds. Proactive capacity management means monitoring trends and alerting before problems impact users, not just reacting to outages.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: Which SNMP version introduced 64-bit counters to address the limitation of 32-bit counters wrapping around too quickly on high-speed interfaces?
A) SNMPv1
B) SNMPv2c
C) SNMPv3
D) SNMP Trap v2
Correct: B
Explanation: SNMPv2c introduced 64-bit counters (Counter64) specifically to handle high-speed interfaces where 32-bit counters would wrap around (overflow) too quickly, causing inaccurate polling results. SNMPv1 only had 32-bit counters, which wrap approximately every 4 billion counts — problematic on gigabit interfaces. SNMPv3 retained the 64-bit counters from v2 and added security features.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A network administrator configures log aggregation to send device logs to a central syslog server using UDP port 514. What is a known limitation of this transport method?
A) UDP requires authentication before log delivery
B) UDP does not guarantee log message delivery
C) UDP syslog cannot transport severity levels above 4
D) UDP limits syslog to RFC 3164 format only
Correct: B
Explanation: UDP is connectionless and does not guarantee delivery, so syslog messages sent over UDP port 514 can be dropped without the sender or receiver being notified. TCP-based syslog (often port 601 or 6514 for TLS) provides reliable delivery confirmation. For security-critical logs, TCP or TLS-based syslog should be used to ensure no events are silently lost.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: A network administrator observes a high number of "runts" on a switch interface. What does this indicate?
A) Packets exceeding the maximum frame size
B) Packets smaller than the minimum valid Ethernet frame size (64 bytes)
C) Broadcast packets flooding the network segment
D) SNMP polling intervals set too aggressively
Correct: B
Explanation: Runts are Ethernet frames smaller than 64 bytes (the minimum valid frame size), often caused by collisions in half-duplex environments or duplex mismatch. Packets exceeding maximum frame size are called "giants" or "jumbo frames." Runts on a full-duplex switch interface often indicate a duplex mismatch — one end operating at half-duplex.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: An OID of 1.3.6.1.2.1.2.2.1.10 is used in an SNMP query. What does the hierarchical structure of this OID represent?
A) A randomly assigned device identifier
B) A specific object within the MIB tree hierarchy
C) An encrypted community string
D) A NetFlow version identifier
Correct: B
Explanation: An OID (Object Identifier) is a sequence of integers separated by dots that uniquely identifies a specific managed object within the MIB hierarchy (in this case, ifInOctets — inbound bytes on an interface). The structure is hierarchical: 1.3.6.1.2.1 is the MIB-II standard, 2 is the interfaces group, and further numbers identify specific objects and instances. OIDs are like postal addresses navigating the MIB tree.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A network diagram that shows the logical relationships between network devices, including IP addressing, VLANs, and routing domains, but not physical cable paths, is called what?
A) Physical network diagram
B) Rack diagram
C) Logical network diagram
D) Floor plan
Correct: C
Explanation: A logical network diagram represents the network's logical structure — IP addressing schemes, VLANs, routing protocols, and device relationships — without depicting physical locations or cable runs. A physical diagram shows actual device locations, cable paths, and port connections. Think: logical = "how traffic flows," physical = "where things are and how they connect physically."

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A technician needs to document the exact U-position of each server, switch, and patch panel within an equipment cabinet. Which type of documentation should be created?
A) Floor plan
B) Rack diagram
C) Logical network diagram
D) Wiring diagram
Correct: B
Explanation: A rack diagram is a detailed vertical representation of equipment mounted in a rack or cabinet, showing the exact position (U-space) of each device, along with power connections and cable management. A floor plan shows the physical layout of rooms and equipment placement within a facility, not the internal layout of individual racks. Rack diagrams are essential for capacity planning and maintenance work.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: Before making changes to a production network firewall, an engineer must complete a formal request that includes risk assessment, rollback procedure, and approval from the change advisory board. This is an example of which process?
A) Incident response
B) Change management
C) Disaster recovery
D) Business continuity planning
Correct: B
Explanation: Change management is the formal process for requesting, reviewing, approving, and documenting changes to production systems to minimize risk and unplanned outages. Incident response is the process for responding to security incidents after they occur, not for planned changes. Change management's key components: change request, risk assessment, rollback plan, approval, implementation, and documentation.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: An organization creates a document that defines acceptable uses of company IT resources, including prohibitions on accessing inappropriate websites and using company equipment for personal business. What is this document called?
A) Non-Disclosure Agreement
B) Acceptable Use Policy
C) BYOD Policy
D) Password Policy
Correct: B
Explanation: An Acceptable Use Policy (AUP) defines what employees are and are not permitted to do with company IT resources, networks, and equipment. An NDA (Non-Disclosure Agreement) is a legal contract preventing disclosure of confidential information to third parties. AUPs are typically signed during onboarding and set the rules of engagement for technology use.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A document that specifies performance guarantees between a service provider and customer, including metrics like uptime percentage, response times, and support ticket resolution times, is called what?
A) NDA
B) BCP
C) SLA
D) AUP
Correct: C
Explanation: A Service Level Agreement (SLA) is a contractual commitment from a service provider defining measurable performance standards such as 99.9% uptime, maximum response times, and penalty provisions if standards are not met. An NDA protects confidential information. SLAs are the "performance contract" — if the provider doesn't meet them, there are typically financial consequences.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: An employee is allowed to use their personal smartphone to access corporate email and applications. The policy governing the security requirements, acceptable use, and data handling for this personal device is called what?
A) AUP
B) BYOD policy
C) NDA
D) Onboarding policy
Correct: B
Explanation: A BYOD (Bring Your Own Device) policy defines the rules, security requirements (such as MDM enrollment and screen locks), and acceptable use conditions for personally owned devices accessing corporate resources. An AUP governs use of company-owned resources, while BYOD specifically addresses personally owned devices. BYOD policies balance employee convenience with corporate security requirements.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: Which document type records the physical location of network cables, including cable IDs, source and destination ports, and cable types, and is essential for troubleshooting and moves/adds/changes?
A) Logical network diagram
B) Site survey report
C) Wiring diagram
D) Rack diagram
Correct: C
Explanation: A wiring diagram (or cabling diagram) documents the physical cable infrastructure, including cable IDs, the specific ports each cable connects, and cable specifications — critical for troubleshooting and managing physical changes. A rack diagram shows device positioning within cabinets but not the complete cable path documentation. Accurate wiring documentation can reduce troubleshooting time from hours to minutes.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A company experiences a major server room fire and must restore operations. The document that defines how the organization will maintain business functions during and after the disaster is called what?
A) Disaster Recovery Plan
B) Incident Response Plan
C) Business Continuity Plan
D) Change Management Policy
Correct: C
Explanation: A Business Continuity Plan (BCP) defines how an organization maintains critical business functions during and after a disruptive event, including alternate operating procedures and communication plans. A Disaster Recovery Plan (DRP) is a subset of BCP that specifically focuses on restoring IT systems and infrastructure. BCP is broader — it covers the entire business; DRP focuses on IT recovery.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A document that captures the radio frequency (RF) coverage, signal strength measurements, channel utilization, and interference sources in a facility before deploying a wireless network is called what?
A) Wiring diagram
B) Site survey report
C) Baseline configuration
D) Audit report
Correct: B
Explanation: A site survey report documents the results of a wireless site survey, including RF coverage maps, signal strength measurements (RSSI), noise floor, channel utilization, and interference sources to inform optimal AP placement. A baseline configuration is a documented standard configuration state for devices, not an RF environment analysis. Site surveys should be conducted before deployment and after significant physical changes.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A network security team conducts a review to verify that all network devices comply with the organization's security standards and identifies deviations. The resulting document is best described as what?
A) Baseline configuration
B) Change management record
C) Audit and assessment report
D) Incident response plan
Correct: C
Explanation: An audit and assessment report documents the findings of a compliance review, identifying gaps between actual device configurations and organizational security standards or regulatory requirements. A baseline configuration is the reference standard being compared against, not the results of the comparison. Audit reports drive remediation activities and demonstrate due diligence to regulators.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A standardized, approved configuration template for all new router deployments — including security hardening, SNMP settings, and NTP servers — is best described as what type of document?
A) Audit report
B) Baseline configuration
C) Site survey
D) Incident response plan
Correct: B
Explanation: A baseline configuration is a documented, approved standard configuration that serves as the reference state for device deployments and compliance checks. An audit report compares current configurations against the baseline to find deviations. Baseline configurations ensure consistency, reduce misconfiguration risk, and provide a known-good state for recovery.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A legal agreement between two organizations that prevents either party from disclosing confidential information shared during a business partnership is called what?
A) SLA
B) AUP
C) NDA
D) BCP
Correct: C
Explanation: A Non-Disclosure Agreement (NDA) is a legally binding contract that restricts parties from sharing confidential information with unauthorized third parties. An SLA defines service performance commitments between a provider and customer. NDAs are often signed before sharing sensitive technical or business information during vendor evaluations or partnerships.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A new employee joins the company and must complete security awareness training, sign the AUP, receive their credentials, and have their equipment provisioned. This process is called what?
A) Change management
B) Onboarding
C) Offboarding
D) Incident response
Correct: B
Explanation: Onboarding is the structured process of integrating a new employee into the organization, including provisioning accounts, assigning equipment, conducting training, and having policies signed. Offboarding is the reverse process when an employee leaves, focusing on revoking access and recovering assets. Proper onboarding documentation ensures consistent security practices from day one.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A document that defines minimum password length, complexity requirements, history restrictions, and expiration periods for all user accounts is an example of which policy?
A) AUP
B) BYOD policy
C) Password policy
D) Incident response plan
Correct: C
Explanation: A password policy defines the technical and procedural requirements for passwords, including minimum length, character complexity, reuse restrictions, and maximum age. An AUP broadly governs IT resource usage but does not typically specify technical password parameters. Password policies are enforced through Active Directory Group Policy Objects (GPOs) or identity management systems.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A document that outlines the steps to take when a security breach is detected, including roles, responsibilities, containment procedures, and escalation paths is called what?
A) Business Continuity Plan
B) Incident Response Plan
C) Disaster Recovery Plan
D) Change Management Policy
Correct: B
Explanation: An Incident Response Plan (IRP) defines the organized approach to addressing and managing security incidents, including preparation, detection, containment, eradication, recovery, and lessons learned phases. A BCP addresses broader operational continuity during disruptions, not specifically cybersecurity incident handling. The NIST incident response lifecycle (Prepare, Detect, Contain, Recover) is a common framework for IRPs.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: When an employee leaves the organization, their Active Directory account is disabled, VPN certificates are revoked, and access badges are deactivated. This is an example of which process?
A) Onboarding
B) Change management
C) Offboarding
D) Incident response
Correct: C
Explanation: Offboarding is the structured process of removing an employee's access to all organizational systems, recovering company assets, and ensuring no unauthorized access remains after departure. Onboarding provisions access; offboarding revokes it. Timely offboarding is critical — former employees with active credentials are a significant security risk and a common audit finding.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A floor plan document shows the locations of network closets, server rooms, cable pathways, and wall jacks throughout a building. How does this differ from a rack diagram?
A) A floor plan shows logical IP addressing while a rack diagram shows physical connections
B) A floor plan shows building-level equipment placement while a rack diagram shows equipment within individual cabinets
C) A floor plan documents wireless coverage while a rack diagram documents wired connections
D) A floor plan is used for change management while a rack diagram is used for disaster recovery
Correct: B
Explanation: A floor plan provides a bird's-eye view of equipment locations within a physical space (rooms, buildings, cable pathways), while a rack diagram provides a detailed vertical view of equipment stacked within individual equipment cabinets (U-space assignments). Both are physical documentation types but at different scales. Together they provide complete physical infrastructure documentation.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A service provider guarantees 99.9% uptime in their SLA. How much total downtime per year does this represent?
A) Approximately 52 minutes
B) Approximately 8.76 hours
C) Approximately 43.8 hours
D) Approximately 87.6 hours
Correct: B
Explanation: 99.9% uptime means 0.1% downtime: 8,760 hours/year × 0.001 = 8.76 hours of allowable downtime per year (approximately 10 minutes per day). 99.99% (four nines) would be about 52 minutes per year. Knowing SLA math is essential for selecting appropriate providers: each additional "nine" reduces allowable downtime by roughly 90%.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A network diagram uses cloud symbols to represent the internet, rectangles for routers, and cylinders for databases, without showing physical cable runs. This is best described as which diagram type?
A) Physical network diagram
B) Rack diagram
C) Logical network diagram
D) Wiring diagram
Correct: C
Explanation: A logical network diagram uses standardized symbols to represent devices and their logical relationships, focusing on how data flows and how devices are logically connected, not where cables physically run. A physical diagram would show actual cable paths, distances, and physical port connections. Logical diagrams are most useful for understanding routing, VLANs, and network segmentation design.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Manage network services
Question: A host sends a broadcast to discover a DHCP server. The server responds with an available IP address offer. The host formally requests that address, and the server acknowledges and confirms the lease. What is this process called?
A) DORA
B) ARP resolution
C) DNS recursion
D) BOOTP negotiation
Correct: A
Explanation: The DHCP DORA process consists of four messages: Discover (client broadcast), Offer (server proposes an IP), Request (client formally requests the offered IP), and Acknowledge (server confirms the lease). ARP is used to resolve IP addresses to MAC addresses after an IP is already assigned. DORA is the foundational DHCP process — every device joining a network goes through it.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Manage network services
Question: A DHCP scope is configured with a range of 192.168.1.100 to 192.168.1.200. An administrator needs the server to always assign IP address 192.168.1.50 to a specific printer based on its MAC address. What DHCP feature accomplishes this?
A) DHCP exclusion range
B) DHCP reservation
C) DHCP relay agent
D) DHCP option 006
Correct: B
Explanation: A DHCP reservation (also called a static mapping) associates a specific IP address with a client's MAC address, ensuring that client always receives the same IP address from the DHCP server. An exclusion range removes addresses from the pool so they are not dynamically assigned, but does not tie them to specific clients. Reservations provide the convenience of DHCP management with the predictability of static assignment.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Manage network services
Question: Client workstations on VLAN 20 are unable to obtain IP addresses from the DHCP server located on VLAN 1. DHCP Discover packets are broadcasts that cannot cross router boundaries. What device/feature is needed to resolve this?
A) DHCP scope expansion
B) DHCP relay agent (IP helper)
C) DHCP reservation
D) Additional DHCP server on VLAN 20
Correct: B
Explanation: A DHCP relay agent (configured with the "ip helper-address" command on Cisco routers) forwards DHCP broadcast packets as unicast to the DHCP server on a different subnet, allowing a single DHCP server to serve multiple VLANs. Adding a separate DHCP server to each VLAN would work but creates unnecessary management overhead. DHCP relay is the standard enterprise solution for multi-VLAN DHCP.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Manage network services
Question: DHCP option 003 is configured on a scope. What information does this option provide to clients?
A) DNS server address
B) Domain name
C) Default gateway (router) address
D) TFTP server address
Correct: C
Explanation: DHCP option 003 provides the default router (default gateway) address to clients, which is essential for routing traffic outside the local subnet. Option 006 provides DNS server addresses, option 015 provides the domain name, and option 066 provides the TFTP server name for PXE booting. Remembering that option 003 = gateway and option 006 = DNS are the two most critical DHCP options to know.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Manage network services
Question: A DHCP scope has a lease time set to 8 hours. A laptop checked out at 9 AM will have its lease expire at what time, and what happens if the user is still connected?
A) 5 PM; the laptop loses connectivity immediately
B) 5 PM; the laptop attempts to renew the lease before expiration
C) 9 PM the next day; leases automatically extend
D) The lease never expires while the laptop is connected
Correct: B
Explanation: At 50% of the lease time (4 hours, at 1 PM), the client attempts to renew with the original DHCP server via unicast; at 87.5% (7 hours, at 4 PM) it broadcasts to any DHCP server if the first renewal failed.
