Question: A network engineer needs to identify all devices on the network and automatically discover their makes, models, software versions, and network neighbors using a non-intrusive, vendor-standard discovery method. Which protocol enables this?
A) SNMP polling all OIDs
B) CDP/LLDP neighbor discovery combined with SNMP
C) NetFlow collection
D) Syslog aggregation
Correct: B
Explanation: CDP (Cisco Discovery Protocol) and LLDP (Link Layer Discovery Protocol, IEEE 802.1AB) enable devices to advertise their identity, capabilities, and network connections to directly connected neighbors — combined with SNMP for detailed device information, this enables comprehensive network topology discovery. NetFlow collects traffic flow data, not device topology information. LLDP is the vendor-neutral standard; CDP is Cisco-proprietary but widely supported.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.1 — Given a scenario, use statistics and sensors to ensure network availability
Question: An SNMP Inform message differs from an SNMP Trap in which important way?
A) Informs are sent by the manager to the agent; Traps are sent by agents to the manager
B) Informs require acknowledgment from the receiver; Traps are unreliable fire-and-forget messages
C) Informs use TCP while Traps use UDP exclusively
D) Informs are only available in SNMPv1; Traps are available in all versions
Correct: B
Explanation: SNMP Informs (introduced in SNMPv2c) require the receiver to send an acknowledgment; if no acknowledgment is received, the sender retransmits the Inform. Standard Traps are unacknowledged (fire-and-forget) over UDP and can be silently lost. Informs provide guaranteed delivery at the cost of more overhead. For critical network events, Informs are preferred over Traps where supported.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.3 — Manage network services
Question: Which DNS record type holds the name server records that delegate a subdomain or zone to specific authoritative name servers?
A) SOA
B) NS
C) PTR
D) CNAME
Correct: B
Explanation: NS (Name Server) records specify which DNS servers are authoritative for a domain or delegated zone; they are found both at the registry level (pointing to your authoritative servers) and within the zone file itself. SOA specifies the primary server and zone parameters, while NS records list all authoritative servers. DNS delegation is accomplished by creating NS records at the parent zone pointing to the child zone's authoritative servers.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.4 — Explain common high availability and disaster recovery concepts
Question: An organization's systems are grouped by criticality. Tier 1 (life safety) systems must restore within 1 hour with no data loss. Tier 2 (core business) must restore within 4 hours with up to 1 hour of data loss. These targets represent which two DR metrics respectively?
A) MTBF and MTTR
B) RTO and RPO
C) SLA and NDA
D) BCP and DRP
Correct: B
Explanation: The 1-hour and 4-hour recovery time targets are RTOs (Recovery Time Objectives), while "no data loss" and "up to 1 hour data loss" are RPOs (Recovery Point Objectives). MTBF measures reliability (failure frequency) and MTTR measures repair time, both applying to individual component metrics rather than business recovery objectives. RTO and RPO are the two fundamental metrics that drive all DR planning decisions and technology choices.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.5 — Use the appropriate network discovery, monitoring, or management tool
Question: An administrator wants to continuously monitor a server's response time and alert when it exceeds 200ms, without deploying an agent on the server. Which monitoring approach requires no agent installation?
A) SNMP polling of server OIDs
B) Agentless ICMP ping-based response time monitoring
C) NetFlow collection from the server
D) Syslog forwarding from the server
Correct: B
Explanation: ICMP ping-based monitoring sends ping probes and measures round-trip time entirely from the monitoring system without requiring any software on the target server — truly agentless. SNMP polling requires an SNMP agent (daemon) configured on the server. ICMP monitoring is the simplest form of availability checking but only measures network reachability, not application health.

Domain: 3.0 Network Operations
Sub-objective: 3.2 — Compare and contrast organizational documentation and policies
Question: A company creates and maintains a document that describes how the organization will respond when an employee reports a potential phishing email, including roles, evidence collection steps, and escalation procedures. Which document type is this?
A) BCP
B) Change management policy
C) Incident response plan
D) Audit report
Correct: C
Explanation: An incident response plan defines the structured approach to detecting, containing, eradicating, and recovering from security incidents, including specific playbooks for common incident types like phishing. A BCP addresses broader business continuity during major disruptions, not specific security incident handling. IRP playbooks for specific scenarios (phishing, ransomware, data breach) allow responders to act quickly without having to improvise under pressure.
Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which component of the CIA triad ensures that data is accessible to authorized users when they need it?
A) Confidentiality
B) Integrity
C) Availability
D) Authentication
Correct: C
Explanation: Availability ensures that systems, networks, and data are accessible to authorized users whenever required. Confidentiality is often confused with availability, but confidentiality focuses on preventing unauthorized access rather than ensuring access for authorized users. The CIA triad forms the foundational model for information security policy: Confidentiality, Integrity, and Availability.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A security architect designs a network where every access request is verified regardless of whether the user is inside or outside the corporate perimeter. Which security model best describes this approach?
A) Defense in depth
B) Zero trust
C) Least privilege
D) Network segmentation
Correct: B
Explanation: Zero trust operates on the principle of "never trust, always verify," requiring authentication and authorization for every access request regardless of network location. Defense in depth uses layered security controls but does not inherently eliminate implicit trust for internal users. Zero trust assumes breach and treats every request as potentially hostile, making it effective against lateral movement by attackers.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which security principle involves implementing multiple overlapping layers of security controls so that if one layer fails, others continue to protect the asset?
A) Zero trust
B) Least privilege
C) Defense in depth
D) Separation of duties
Correct: C
Explanation: Defense in depth applies multiple, redundant security layers such as firewalls, IDS, endpoint protection, and physical security so that a single control failure does not compromise the entire system. Zero trust is a related but distinct model focused on eliminating implicit trust rather than layering defenses. The concept is analogous to a medieval castle with a moat, walls, guards, and locked doors — each layer adds friction for an attacker.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A user account is given only the permissions required to perform their specific job function and no more. Which security principle is being applied?
A) Defense in depth
B) Separation of duties
C) Zero trust
D) Least privilege
Correct: D
Explanation: Least privilege restricts user accounts and processes to the minimum permissions necessary to perform their intended functions, limiting the damage from compromised credentials or insider threats. Separation of duties divides a task among multiple people to prevent fraud but does not directly govern the scope of individual permissions. Least privilege reduces the attack surface and limits lateral movement if an account is compromised.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A company separates its guest Wi-Fi network from its corporate LAN using VLANs so that guest traffic cannot reach internal servers. This is an example of which concept?
A) Honeypotting
B) Authentication hardening
C) Network segmentation
D) Defense in depth
Correct: C
Explanation: Network segmentation divides a network into distinct zones, limiting the ability of traffic in one segment to reach resources in another, thereby containing breaches and reducing attack surface. Defense in depth could encompass segmentation but is a broader strategy; here the specific technique being applied is segmentation. VLANs provide logical segmentation, while physical segmentation uses separate hardware; both achieve the same goal of isolating traffic.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which type of decoy system is deployed on a network to attract and detect malicious activity by mimicking a legitimate target?
A) Bastion host
B) Jump server
C) Honeypot
D) Proxy server
Correct: C
Explanation: A honeypot is a decoy system intentionally made to look attractive to attackers, designed to detect, deflect, or study unauthorized access attempts. A bastion host is a hardened server exposed to the internet to provide specific services, not a decoy. Honeypots provide valuable threat intelligence by logging attacker tactics and tools without risking production systems.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A security team deploys multiple interconnected honeypots across several network segments to create a realistic-looking fake environment for attackers to explore. What is this called?
A) DMZ
B) Honeynet
C) Sandbox
D) VLAN
Correct: B
Explanation: A honeynet is a network of honeypots that simulates a full production environment, allowing security teams to observe sophisticated attacker behavior across multiple systems. A sandbox isolates applications or code for testing but is not specifically designed as an attacker decoy. Honeynets provide richer threat intelligence than single honeypots because they capture multi-stage attack campaigns.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which authentication protocol uses a centralized server to provide Authentication, Authorization, and Accounting (AAA) services and is commonly used for network device administration?
A) LDAP
B) Kerberos
C) TACACS+
D) RADIUS
Correct: C
Explanation: TACACS+ (Terminal Access Controller Access-Control System Plus) is a Cisco-developed AAA protocol that separates authentication, authorization, and accounting into distinct functions and is widely used for managing access to network devices. RADIUS also provides AAA but combines authentication and authorization into one process and is more commonly used for network access control. TACACS+ uses TCP port 49 and encrypts the entire payload, making it preferred for device administration.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which authentication protocol is most commonly used to authenticate remote access users connecting to a network and runs over UDP?
A) TACACS+
B) RADIUS
C) Kerberos
D) LDAP
Correct: B
Explanation: RADIUS (Remote Authentication Dial-In User Service) uses UDP ports 1812 and 1813 and is the standard protocol for authenticating remote access users such as those connecting via VPN or wireless. TACACS+ uses TCP and is preferred for device administration rather than user remote access. RADIUS encrypts only the password field, while TACACS+ encrypts the entire packet body.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A directory service protocol used to query and modify user account information stored in a directory, often used for enterprise authentication. Which protocol is this?
A) RADIUS
B) SNMP
C) LDAP
D) TACACS+
Correct: C
Explanation: LDAP (Lightweight Directory Access Protocol) is used to access and manage directory information services such as Microsoft Active Directory, providing a standard way to look up user credentials and attributes. RADIUS handles authentication decisions but relies on a backend directory like LDAP to store user information. LDAP operates on TCP port 389, while LDAPS (LDAP over SSL) uses port 636.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which authentication protocol uses tickets issued by a Key Distribution Center (KDC) to allow single sign-on within a domain environment?
A) RADIUS
B) Kerberos
C) LDAP
D) SAML
Correct: B
Explanation: Kerberos uses a trusted third party called the KDC, which issues Ticket Granting Tickets (TGTs) and service tickets to allow users to authenticate to multiple services without re-entering credentials. LDAP provides directory lookup services but does not handle ticket-based authentication. Kerberos is the default authentication protocol in Windows Active Directory environments and uses port 88.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A user logs into their corporate portal once and gains access to email, HR systems, and project management tools without re-entering credentials. Which authentication method is being used?
A) MFA
B) Certificate-based authentication
C) SSO
D) 802.1X
Correct: C
Explanation: Single Sign-On (SSO) allows users to authenticate once and access multiple applications or services without repeated login prompts, improving user experience while centralizing authentication management. MFA adds additional verification factors but does not eliminate the need to authenticate to each service separately unless combined with SSO. SSO reduces password fatigue and attack surface by limiting the number of credentials users must manage.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which authentication method requires a user to provide something they know and something they have before being granted access?
A) SSO
B) RBAC
C) MFA
D) LDAP
Correct: C
Explanation: Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) requires two or more verification factors from different categories: something you know (password), something you have (token), and something you are (biometric). SSO streamlines the login experience but is not an authentication factor itself. MFA significantly reduces the risk of account compromise from stolen passwords because an attacker would need the additional factor as well.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which IEEE standard defines port-based Network Access Control, requiring devices to authenticate before being allowed access to the network?
A) 802.11
B) 802.3
C) 802.1X
D) 802.1Q
Correct: C
Explanation: IEEE 802.1X is a port-based Network Access Control (NAC) standard that requires supplicants (clients) to authenticate via an authenticator (switch/AP) to an authentication server (RADIUS) before network access is granted. 802.1Q defines VLAN tagging and is unrelated to access control. 802.1X is commonly used alongside RADIUS and EAP to enforce that only authorized devices connect to wired or wireless networks.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A network administrator assigns permissions to users based on their job title rather than individual accounts, making access management easier to scale. Which authorization model is this?
A) Rules-based access control
B) Mandatory access control
C) Role-based access control
D) Discretionary access control
Correct: C
Explanation: Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) grants permissions based on predefined roles associated with job functions, so that all users in the same role receive the same access rights. Rules-based access control applies conditions or criteria (such as time of day or IP address) to access decisions rather than using organizational roles. RBAC simplifies administration because changing a role's permissions updates access for all users assigned to that role simultaneously.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which authorization method grants or denies access based on conditions such as time of day, source IP address, or specific network interface rather than a user's organizational role?
A) RBAC
B) Rules-based access control
C) SSO
D) Least privilege
Correct: B
Explanation: Rules-based access control applies a set of conditions or policies to every access request, allowing access only when the defined rules are satisfied, regardless of the user's role. RBAC assigns access based on job roles and does not inherently evaluate contextual conditions like time or location. Rules-based access control is commonly implemented in firewall ACLs and router policies where conditions define what traffic is permitted.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A digital credential stored on a user's device that contains their public key, identity information, and a digital signature from a trusted Certificate Authority is used to authenticate them. What is this?
A) Pre-shared key
B) RADIUS token
C) Digital certificate
D) Kerberos ticket
Correct: C
Explanation: A digital certificate binds a public key to an identity and is signed by a Certificate Authority (CA) to prove authenticity, enabling certificate-based authentication. A Kerberos ticket grants access to specific services within a domain but is not a long-term credential stored on a device. Certificate-based authentication is considered more secure than passwords because private keys never leave the device and certificates can be revoked centrally.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Which security concept involves ensuring that data has not been altered or corrupted in an unauthorized manner, and is often verified using hashing algorithms?
A) Availability
B) Confidentiality
C) Non-repudiation
D) Integrity
Correct: D
Explanation: Integrity ensures data remains accurate and unmodified from its original state, with hashing algorithms like SHA-256 providing a way to detect any changes. Confidentiality protects data from unauthorized access but does not verify whether the data itself has been modified. A common memory aid: integrity is about the data being what it claims to be, while confidentiality is about who can see it.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: A company configures its authentication system so that even if a user's password is compromised, an attacker still cannot log in without access to the user's registered mobile device. Which principle is being applied?
A) Least privilege
B) Defense in depth
C) MFA
D) Zero trust
Correct: C
Explanation: MFA requires more than one form of verification, so a stolen password alone is insufficient to gain access without the second factor such as a one-time code sent to a registered mobile device. Defense in depth is a broader strategy that could include MFA as one layer, but the specific mechanism described here is MFA. The second factor transforms the mobile device into something you have, adding a physical barrier that a remote attacker cannot easily bypass.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.1 — Explain common security concepts
Question: Physical separation of network segments using different switches, routers, or cables rather than VLAN tags describes which type of segmentation?
A) Logical segmentation
B) Virtual segmentation
C) Physical segmentation
D) Micro-segmentation
Correct: C
Explanation: Physical segmentation uses separate physical hardware to isolate network segments, providing the strongest form of isolation because traffic cannot cross segments without passing through a routing device. Logical segmentation uses VLANs on shared hardware and relies on software enforcement, which can be bypassed through VLAN hopping attacks. Physical segmentation is commonly used in high-security environments such as classified government networks where air gaps are required.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker sends a massive volume of SYN packets to a web server without completing the TCP three-way handshake, exhausting the server's connection table. Which attack is this?
A) UDP flood
B) Ping of death
C) SYN flood
D) Amplification attack
Correct: C
Explanation: A SYN flood exploits the TCP handshake by sending SYN packets and never responding to the server's SYN-ACK, filling the half-open connection table until the server can no longer accept legitimate connections. A UDP flood sends large volumes of UDP datagrams but does not exploit the TCP handshake mechanism. SYN flood attacks are mitigated by SYN cookies, which allow the server to validate connection requests without storing state for each half-open connection.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker sends DNS queries with a spoofed source IP address (the victim's IP) to many open DNS resolvers, causing a large volume of DNS responses to flood the victim. Which attack type is this?
A) DNS poisoning
B) Reflection and amplification attack
C) SYN flood
D) VLAN hopping
Correct: B
Explanation: A reflection attack uses third-party servers to reflect traffic toward a victim, while amplification leverages protocols like DNS where the response is much larger than the request, multiplying the attack volume. DNS poisoning corrupts cached DNS records to redirect users but does not generate a traffic flood against a victim. The amplification factor in DNS attacks can be 50x or more, making small botnets capable of generating enormous attack traffic.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: A network administrator notices that the ARP table on a core switch shows the same MAC address mapped to two different IP addresses — one belonging to the default gateway and one to an unknown device. Which attack is most likely occurring?
A) VLAN hopping
B) ARP spoofing
C) DNS hijacking
D) Rogue DHCP
Correct: B
Explanation: ARP spoofing (ARP poisoning) involves an attacker sending gratuitous ARP replies that associate their MAC address with a legitimate IP address, allowing them to intercept traffic intended for that IP. VLAN hopping allows an attacker to send traffic to a different VLAN but does not involve ARP table manipulation. ARP spoofing is a prerequisite for many on-path (man-in-the-middle) attacks on local networks because it redirects traffic through the attacker's device.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker positions themselves between a client and a server, intercepting and potentially modifying all communications without either party being aware. What type of attack is this?
A) Replay attack
B) On-path (MITM) attack
C) Session hijacking
D) DNS poisoning
Correct: B
Explanation: An on-path attack (also called a man-in-the-middle attack) places the attacker in the communication path so they can intercept, read, and modify data in transit. A replay attack captures authentication tokens and replays them later rather than maintaining a live interception position. On-path attacks are facilitated by ARP spoofing on LANs and can be mitigated by encryption, certificate pinning, and HSTS.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: Users on a network begin receiving incorrect IP addresses for a popular website, leading them to a fraudulent site. Investigation reveals the local DNS resolver's cache has been corrupted. Which attack occurred?
A) DNS zone transfer attack
B) DNS hijacking
C) DNS spoofing/poisoning
D) ARP spoofing
Correct: C
Explanation: DNS poisoning (spoofing) injects false DNS records into a resolver's cache, causing clients to receive incorrect IP addresses and be redirected to attacker-controlled servers. DNS hijacking typically involves modifying DNS settings on a device or router directly rather than corrupting a cache. DNS poisoning is mitigated by DNSSEC, which digitally signs DNS records to prevent cache injection.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker exploits a misconfigured DNS server to request a full copy of a zone's DNS records, obtaining a list of all hostnames, IP addresses, and mail servers for a domain. What is this called?
A) DNS hijacking
B) DNS zone transfer attack
C) DNS amplification
D) DNS poisoning
Correct: B
Explanation: A DNS zone transfer attack exploits improperly configured DNS servers that allow any host to request a zone transfer (AXFR), which returns all DNS records for a zone and reveals the internal network topology. DNS amplification uses DNS responses to flood a victim and does not involve copying zone records. Zone transfers should be restricted to authorized secondary DNS servers only, using ACLs on the DNS server.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker connects an unauthorized switch to a trunk port and uses 802.1Q double-tagging to send traffic into a VLAN they should not have access to. Which attack is this?
A) ARP spoofing
B) VLAN hopping
C) Rogue DHCP
D) Evil twin
Correct: B
Explanation: VLAN hopping allows an attacker to bypass VLAN segmentation by either connecting to a trunk port or using double-tagging to embed a VLAN tag inside another, causing switches to forward traffic to the target VLAN. ARP spoofing operates at Layer 2 but targets the ARP cache rather than VLAN membership. VLAN hopping is prevented by disabling automatic trunk negotiation, using dedicated native VLANs, and pruning unused VLANs from trunk ports.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: A wireless user connects to an access point that has the same SSID as the corporate Wi-Fi but is controlled by an attacker in a nearby vehicle. Which attack is being executed?
A) Deauthentication attack
B) Rogue DHCP
C) Evil twin
D) VLAN hopping
Correct: C
Explanation: An evil twin attack uses a rogue access point broadcasting the same SSID as a legitimate network, tricking users into connecting to the attacker's AP where their traffic can be intercepted. A deauthentication attack forces clients to disconnect from a legitimate AP but is often a precursor to an evil twin attack rather than the attack itself. Evil twin attacks are mitigated by WPA3-Enterprise with 802.1X authentication, where clients validate the AP's certificate before connecting.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker sets up an unauthorized DHCP server on the network and responds to client DHCP requests faster than the legitimate server, providing clients with a malicious default gateway IP. Which attack is this?
A) VLAN hopping
B) ARP spoofing
C) DNS poisoning
D) Rogue DHCP
Correct: D
Explanation: A rogue DHCP attack involves an unauthorized DHCP server responding to client requests and assigning network configuration that routes traffic through the attacker's controlled gateway. ARP spoofing also redirects traffic but works at Layer 2 by corrupting ARP caches rather than leveraging DHCP. Rogue DHCP is mitigated by DHCP snooping, which blocks DHCP server responses from untrusted switch ports.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker sends forged 802.11 management frames to force wireless clients off the network, causing repeated disconnections. What type of attack is this?
A) Evil twin
B) Deauthentication attack
C) UDP flood
D) SYN flood
Correct: B
Explanation: A deauthentication attack floods clients with forged deauthentication frames, forcing them to disconnect from the access point, which can be used as a denial of service or as a precursor to an evil twin attack. An evil twin uses a rogue AP rather than forged management frames to disconnect clients. 802.11w (Protected Management Frames) mitigates deauthentication attacks by requiring management frames to be authenticated.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker systematically tries every possible password combination for a user account until the correct one is found. Which attack type is this?
A) Dictionary attack
B) Credential harvesting
C) Password spraying
D) Brute force attack
Correct: D
Explanation: A brute force attack exhaustively tries all possible character combinations to discover a password, guaranteeing success eventually but requiring significant time and computational resources. A dictionary attack is more targeted, using a wordlist of common passwords and is faster but may miss complex passwords not in the list. Brute force attacks are mitigated by account lockout policies, long complex passwords, and MFA.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker uses a list of commonly used passwords such as "Password1" and "Summer2024" and tries each one against thousands of different user accounts to avoid triggering lockout policies. This describes which attack?
A) Brute force
B) Dictionary attack
C) Password spraying
D) Credential harvesting
Correct: C
Explanation: Password spraying tests a small number of common passwords across a large number of accounts, staying below lockout thresholds while still having a high chance of success given that many users choose predictable passwords. A dictionary attack focuses many password attempts against a single account rather than spreading attempts across many accounts. Password spraying is detected by monitoring for distributed failed login attempts across multiple accounts rather than repeated failures on one account.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker sends an email appearing to come from a user's bank, asking them to click a link and enter their login credentials on a fake website. Which attack type is this?
A) Vishing
B) Smishing
C) Spear phishing
D) Phishing
Correct: D
Explanation: Phishing uses deceptive emails that impersonate trusted entities to trick users into revealing credentials or installing malware. Vishing uses voice calls and smishing uses SMS messages for the same purpose. Phishing is mitigated by user security awareness training, email filtering, and multi-factor authentication that makes stolen credentials alone insufficient for access.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker calls an employee pretending to be from the IT help desk and tricks them into revealing their password. Which type of social engineering attack is this?
A) Phishing
B) Smishing
C) Vishing
D) Spear phishing
Correct: C
Explanation: Vishing (voice phishing) uses telephone calls to manipulate victims into providing sensitive information or performing actions that benefit the attacker. Phishing uses email rather than voice calls as the attack vector. Vishing attacks often exploit urgency and authority (e.g., impersonating IT support or executives) to bypass the victim's critical thinking.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An employee with authorized access to customer data downloads and sells it to a competitor. Which threat category does this represent?
A) Ransomware attack
B) Insider threat
C) Credential harvesting
D) Social engineering
Correct: B
Explanation: An insider threat involves malicious actions taken by individuals with legitimate access to organizational systems, including employees, contractors, or partners who misuse their privileges. Social engineering manipulates people from outside the organization rather than leveraging existing authorized access. Insider threats are particularly dangerous because legitimate access makes malicious activity harder to detect through perimeter security controls.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: A malicious program encrypts all files on an infected workstation and demands payment in cryptocurrency for the decryption key. Which type of attack is this?
A) Credential harvesting
B) Spyware
C) Ransomware
D) Worm
Correct: C
Explanation: Ransomware encrypts victim's data and extorts payment for decryption keys, making data inaccessible until either the ransom is paid or backups are restored. Credential harvesting focuses on stealing authentication information rather than encrypting data. Ransomware is mitigated by offline backups, endpoint detection and response (EDR) tools, and limiting user privileges to prevent widespread encryption.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker sends a single UDP packet to the broadcast address of a network with the victim's IP as the source, causing all hosts to reply to the victim simultaneously. What is this called?
A) SYN flood
B) Smurf attack (ICMP amplification)
C) Teardrop attack
D) Ping of death
Correct: B
Explanation: A Smurf attack sends ICMP echo requests to a network broadcast address with a spoofed source IP of the victim, causing all hosts on the network to send ICMP replies to the victim, overwhelming it. A SYN flood targets TCP connections rather than using ICMP. Smurf attacks are prevented by configuring routers to block directed broadcasts and disabling IP-directed broadcast forwarding.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker uses a large botnet to send enough legitimate-looking HTTP GET requests to a website to exhaust its server resources, making it unavailable to real users. What type of attack is this?
A) SYN flood
B) DNS amplification
C) UDP flood
D) Application-layer DDoS
Correct: D
Explanation: An application-layer DDoS attack (Layer 7) uses apparently legitimate requests to exhaust server-side resources such as CPU and memory rather than saturating network bandwidth. A SYN flood operates at Layer 4 by filling the TCP connection table rather than the application request queue. Application-layer DDoS attacks are harder to detect because individual requests appear normal; they are mitigated by rate limiting, CAPTCHAs, and WAFs.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker receives a text message from what appears to be a delivery company asking them to click a link to reschedule a package. The link leads to a credential-harvesting page. What type of attack is this?
A) Vishing
B) Phishing
C) Smishing
D) Spear phishing
Correct: C
Explanation: Smishing (SMS phishing) uses text messages to lure victims into clicking malicious links or providing sensitive information. Vishing uses voice calls rather than text messages. Smishing is effective because users tend to trust SMS messages more than emails and mobile devices often have less security software to detect malicious links.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.2 — Compare and contrast common types of attacks
Question: An attacker uses malware to collect saved browser passwords, email credentials, and session tokens from multiple infected workstations and sends them to a remote server. What is this technique called?
A) Password spraying
B) Brute force
C) Credential harvesting
D) Dictionary attack
Correct: C
Explanation: Credential harvesting uses malware, phishing, or other methods to gather authentication credentials from victims for later use in unauthorized access. Password spraying attempts logins with known common passwords rather than collecting stored credentials. Harvested credentials are often used in credential stuffing attacks against other services where users have reused the same username and password.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network engineer creates a list of rules on a router that permits traffic from specific IP addresses to reach an internal server on port 443 and denies all other traffic. What is this called?
A) Firewall policy
B) DHCP snooping
C) ACL
D) NAC
Correct: C
Explanation: An Access Control List (ACL) is a set of permit or deny rules applied to a router or switch interface that filters traffic based on criteria such as source/destination IP, port, and protocol. A firewall policy is broader and may include stateful inspection, while ACLs are typically stateless filters applied at the router level. ACLs are applied in order, and the first matching rule is executed, so more specific rules should appear before general rules.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A security administrator wants to prevent any device from receiving more than three different MAC addresses on a single switch port. Which hardening technique should be applied?
A) DHCP snooping
B) Dynamic ARP inspection
C) Port security
D) 802.1X
Correct: C
Explanation: Port security limits the number of MAC addresses allowed on a switch port and can shut down or restrict a port if unauthorized MAC addresses are detected. DHCP snooping controls which ports can act as DHCP servers but does not restrict MAC address counts. Port security is commonly configured with a maximum of one or a few MAC addresses per port to prevent MAC flooding attacks.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network switch is configured to only trust DHCP server responses from specific ports connected to legitimate DHCP servers, dropping offers received on all other ports. What feature is this?
A) Dynamic ARP inspection
B) Port security
C) DHCP snooping
D) 802.1X
Correct: C
Explanation: DHCP snooping builds a binding table of legitimate IP-to-MAC-to-port mappings and blocks DHCP server responses from untrusted ports, preventing rogue DHCP attacks. Dynamic ARP inspection uses the DHCP snooping binding table but validates ARP packets rather than DHCP messages. DHCP snooping is typically enabled on all access ports with only uplinks to legitimate DHCP servers marked as trusted.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: Which switch security feature validates ARP packets against a trusted database to prevent ARP spoofing attacks?
A) Port security
B) DHCP snooping
C) 802.1X NAC
D) Dynamic ARP inspection
Correct: D
Explanation: Dynamic ARP Inspection (DAI) validates ARP packets against the DHCP snooping binding table, dropping ARP packets with IP-to-MAC mappings that do not match the trusted database, preventing ARP spoofing. DHCP snooping creates the binding table that DAI uses but does not validate ARP traffic. DAI and DHCP snooping are complementary features that together protect against Layer 2 spoofing attacks.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network administrator discovers that all new switches ship with the same default username and password. What is the most important first hardening step?
A) Disable unused ports
B) Enable STP
C) Change default credentials
D) Update firmware
Correct: C
Explanation: Changing default credentials is the most critical first step because default usernames and passwords are publicly known and are the first thing attackers attempt when targeting network devices. Disabling unused ports and updating firmware are also important but do not address the immediate risk of default credential exploitation. Devices with unchanged default credentials are trivially compromised and represent one of the most commonly exploited vulnerabilities.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A security team wants to ensure that known vulnerabilities in network device operating systems are remediated. Which ongoing practice addresses this?
A) Disabling unused protocols
B) Changing default credentials
C) Firmware upgrades and patching
D) Port security
Correct: C
Explanation: Regular firmware upgrades and patching address known vulnerabilities in network device operating systems that manufacturers release fixes for over time. Changing default credentials addresses configuration weaknesses but does not fix software vulnerabilities in the code. A vulnerability management program should track patch levels across all devices and prioritize critical vulnerabilities based on CVSS scores and exposure.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: SNMPv1 and SNMPv2 transmit community strings in plaintext, making them vulnerable to eavesdropping. Which version provides authentication and encryption for SNMP communications?
A) SNMPv2c
B) SNMPv3
C) SNMPv2
D) SNMP over TLS
Correct: B
Explanation: SNMPv3 introduces user-based security with authentication (MD5 or SHA) and privacy (DES or AES encryption), making it the only SNMP version that should be used in security-conscious environments. SNMPv2c uses community strings for access control but transmits them in cleartext. SNMPv3 should be configured with the authPriv security level to enable both authentication and encryption for all SNMP communications.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A wireless network administrator wants to use the strongest available enterprise wireless encryption that supports Simultaneous Authentication of Equals (SAE). Which standard should be configured?
A) WEP
B) WPA2-Personal
C) WPA2-Enterprise
D) WPA3-Enterprise
Correct: D
Explanation: WPA3-Enterprise uses SAE (Simultaneous Authentication of Equals) for improved key exchange security and 192-bit encryption in its highest security mode, making it the strongest enterprise wireless security standard currently available. WPA2-Enterprise provides strong security for many environments but uses the older 4-way handshake vulnerable to offline dictionary attacks. WPA3 protects against the KRACK attack that affected WPA2 and provides forward secrecy through its key exchange mechanism.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network administrator hides the SSID of a corporate wireless network so it does not appear in broadcast beacon frames. What is a key limitation of this approach?
A) It breaks WPA3 encryption
B) It prevents 802.1X from working
C) The SSID is still visible in probe requests and can be discovered by passive scanning
D) It disables MAC address filtering
Correct: C
Explanation: Hiding an SSID only removes it from beacon frames; the SSID is still transmitted in probe request/response frames and can be captured by a wireless analyzer, providing minimal security benefit. MAC filtering and 802.1X are independent access control mechanisms unaffected by SSID broadcasting settings. SSID hiding is considered security through obscurity and should not be relied upon as a primary security control.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A firewall is configured to allow only established TCP sessions initiated from the internal network and block all externally initiated connections. What type of firewall feature is this?
A) Packet filtering
B) Stateful inspection
C) Application-layer filtering
D) NAT
Correct: B
Explanation: Stateful inspection tracks the state of TCP connections and allows return traffic only for sessions that were legitimately established from the inside, blocking externally initiated connections that do not match a known session. Packet filtering evaluates each packet independently without tracking connection state, making it unable to distinguish return traffic from new inbound connections. Stateful firewalls maintain a state table that maps each connection's source, destination, port, and sequence numbers.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A company wants to ensure only devices that meet security compliance standards (current patches, active antivirus) can connect to the network. Which technology enforces this?
A) 802.1Q
B) NAC (Network Access Control)
C) DHCP snooping
D) Port security
Correct: B
Explanation: Network Access Control (NAC) evaluates the health posture of devices attempting to connect to the network and enforces policy by placing non-compliant devices in quarantine VLANs or denying access. Port security limits MAC addresses but does not assess device health or compliance status. NAC is typically implemented using 802.1X as the authentication framework combined with posture assessment agents that check patch levels and security software status.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network administrator wants to prevent Telnet from being used to manage switches and configure a replacement. Which protocol should replace Telnet?
A) HTTP
B) FTP
C) SSH
D) SNMP
Correct: C
Explanation: SSH (Secure Shell) replaces Telnet by providing encrypted command-line access to network devices, preventing credentials and management traffic from being captured in plaintext. HTTP transmits management data unencrypted and should be replaced by HTTPS for web-based management. SSH uses asymmetric key exchange followed by symmetric encryption, protecting management sessions from eavesdropping and modification.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A company restricts network access so that users in the accounting department can only reach accounting servers, and IT staff can reach all systems but no other staff can access IT infrastructure. This is implemented using which concept?
A) Geofencing
B) Zero trust
C) Role-based access
D) Security zones
Correct: C
Explanation: Role-based access restricts network resource access based on a user's organizational role, so that accounting staff reach only accounting resources and IT staff have broader infrastructure access. Security zones define network segments with different trust levels but do not inherently differentiate access based on user role within a zone. Role-based access is often enforced through firewall policies that use group membership information from Active Directory.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A company configures its mobile device management system to restrict access to corporate resources when a device is detected outside of a defined geographic area. What is this capability called?
A) Role-based access
B) Time-based ACL
C) Geofencing
D) NAC
Correct: C
Explanation: Geofencing uses GPS or network location data to define a geographic boundary and restricts access to resources when a device moves outside that boundary. Time-based ACLs restrict access based on time of day rather than physical location. Geofencing is particularly useful for organizations with employees who only need access from specific office locations, reducing the risk of credential misuse from foreign locations.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network administrator notices an old switch in the data center is running a firmware version from five years ago with several known critical vulnerabilities. Which action most directly addresses this risk?
A) Disable unused switch ports
B) Implement port security
C) Upgrade the switch firmware
D) Change the SNMP community string
Correct: C
Explanation: Upgrading the firmware directly remediates the known vulnerabilities by applying manufacturer-supplied patches that fix the security flaws. Disabling unused ports reduces the attack surface but does not fix the underlying vulnerabilities that could be exploited through active ports. A formal patch management process should track firmware versions across all network devices and schedule upgrades based on vulnerability severity and risk.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network contains a server accessible from both the internet and the internal LAN. To limit risk, the administrator places it in a separate network segment where it is isolated from both the internal network and the internet. What is this segment called?
A) Guest VLAN
B) Management VLAN
C) DMZ
D) Quarantine VLAN
Correct: C
Explanation: A DMZ (Demilitarized Zone) is a network segment that sits between the untrusted internet and the trusted internal network, hosting publicly accessible servers while limiting their access to internal resources. A guest VLAN isolates visitor devices from corporate resources but is not specifically designed to host internet-facing servers. The DMZ architecture typically uses two firewalls: one between the internet and DMZ, and one between the DMZ and the internal network.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: MAC address filtering on a wireless network is often considered a weak security control. What is the primary reason for this limitation?
A) It prevents WPA3 from functioning correctly
B) It is not supported by most wireless access points
C) MAC addresses can be spoofed using freely available software
D) It reduces wireless network throughput significantly
Correct: C
Explanation: MAC address filtering can be bypassed trivially because an attacker can use wireless monitoring tools to capture allowed MAC addresses and then spoof that address on their own device. WPA3 compatibility and throughput are unaffected by MAC filtering; the weakness is purely in the ease of circumventing it. MAC filtering should be considered a minor deterrent at best and must not be relied upon as a primary access control for wireless networks.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.3 — Apply network hardening techniques
Question: A network administrator wants to disable all network services and protocols on a switch that are not required for its operation, such as CDP, HTTP management, and unused physical ports. This practice is known as what?
A) Network segmentation
B) ACL implementation
C) Hardening by reducing attack surface
D) VLAN pruning
Correct: C
Explanation: Reducing the attack surface by disabling unnecessary services, protocols, and ports minimizes the number of potential entry points an attacker can exploit on a network device. VLAN pruning specifically removes VLANs from trunk links and is one aspect of this broader practice. Each unnecessary open port or running protocol represents an additional vector for exploitation, so the principle of least functionality dictates that only required services should run.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A company needs to securely connect its headquarters network to its branch office network over the internet so all traffic between them is encrypted. Which VPN type is most appropriate?
A) Client-to-site VPN
B) Clientless VPN
C) Split tunnel VPN
D) Site-to-site VPN
Correct: D
Explanation: A site-to-site VPN creates a permanent encrypted tunnel between two network gateways, allowing hosts at both locations to communicate as if on the same local network. A client-to-site VPN connects individual remote users to the network rather than connecting two fixed sites. Site-to-site VPNs are typically managed by the network infrastructure at each end, requiring no VPN client software on individual workstations.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A remote employee needs to connect their laptop to the corporate network over the internet. Their device will receive a virtual IP address on the corporate subnet. Which VPN type is being used?
A) Site-to-site VPN
B) Client-to-site VPN
C) Clientless VPN
D) GRE tunnel
Correct: B
Explanation: A client-to-site (remote access) VPN connects individual remote clients to the corporate network, assigning them an internal IP address so they can access resources as if physically present in the office. A site-to-site VPN connects entire networks rather than individual clients. Client-to-site VPNs require VPN client software installed on the endpoint device and support protocols like IPSec or SSL/TLS.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: An employee uses only their web browser to access corporate email, file shares, and web applications through an SSL-encrypted portal without installing any VPN software. Which type of VPN access is this?
A) Site-to-site VPN
B) Full tunnel VPN
C) Clientless VPN
D) Split tunnel VPN
Correct: C
Explanation: Clientless VPN provides remote access through an SSL/TLS web portal using only a browser, without requiring a VPN client to be installed on the endpoint. Full tunnel VPN requires client software and routes all traffic through the VPN gateway. Clientless VPN is convenient for unmanaged devices or kiosk scenarios but typically provides access only to web-based applications rather than full network access.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: Which VPN protocol suite operates at Layer 3 and provides both confidentiality and integrity through AH and ESP protocols, commonly used in site-to-site VPNs?
A) L2TP
B) GRE
C) WireGuard
D) IPSec
Correct: D
Explanation: IPSec is a Layer 3 suite of protocols that uses Authentication Header (AH) for integrity and Encapsulating Security Payload (ESP) for confidentiality and integrity, making it the standard for secure site-to-site VPN tunnels. L2TP is a Layer 2 tunneling protocol that lacks encryption by itself and is typically paired with IPSec (L2TP/IPSec). IPSec operates in either transport mode (host-to-host) or tunnel mode (network-to-network) and uses IKE for key negotiation on UDP port 500.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: Which VPN protocol creates a simple tunneling mechanism at Layer 3 without encryption, often used as a transport carrier wrapped inside IPSec for greater security?
A) L2TP
B) GRE
C) SSL/TLS
D) WireGuard
Correct: B
Explanation: GRE (Generic Routing Encapsulation) is a lightweight tunneling protocol that encapsulates packets of one network protocol inside another but provides no encryption or security on its own. L2TP also lacks native encryption but differs from GRE in that it operates at Layer 2 and encapsulates PPP frames. GRE is often combined with IPSec in a GRE over IPSec configuration to carry routing protocols like OSPF or EIGRP securely across WAN links.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A modern VPN protocol that uses the Noise Protocol Framework, offers faster connection setup than IPSec, and has a simpler codebase reducing audit complexity. Which protocol is this?
A) L2TP/IPSec
B) SSL/TLS VPN
C) OpenVPN
D) WireGuard
Correct: D
Explanation: WireGuard is a modern VPN protocol designed with simplicity and performance in mind, using state-of-the-art cryptography and a code base roughly 100 times smaller than OpenVPN or IPSec, reducing the attack surface. OpenVPN is SSL-based and also widely used, but WireGuard offers lower latency and faster handshakes. WireGuard was added to the Linux kernel in version 5.6 and has been adopted by many commercial VPN providers and network vendors.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A remote worker's VPN is configured so that only traffic destined for corporate resources goes through the VPN tunnel, while all other internet traffic goes directly to the internet. What is this configuration called?
A) Full tunnel
B) Hairpin routing
C) Split tunnel
D) Clientless access
Correct: C
Explanation: Split tunneling routes only corporate-bound traffic through the encrypted VPN tunnel while other internet traffic bypasses the VPN and exits directly, reducing VPN gateway load. Full tunnel routes all traffic through the VPN gateway, giving the organization greater visibility and control over the employee's traffic. Split tunneling improves performance for the remote user but means that internet-bound threats are not inspected by corporate security tools.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: An organization requires that all remote worker internet traffic passes through the corporate security stack for inspection, even when the user is browsing non-work websites. Which VPN configuration achieves this?
A) Split tunnel VPN
B) Clientless VPN
C) Full tunnel VPN
D) Site-to-site VPN
Correct: C
Explanation: Full tunnel VPN routes all traffic including personal internet browsing through the corporate VPN gateway, allowing security appliances to inspect and filter all employee traffic. Split tunnel only routes corporate traffic through the VPN and would allow unfiltered internet access. Full tunneling increases VPN gateway load but provides complete traffic visibility and prevents attackers from pivoting through a user's unsecured internet connection into the corporate network.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: An administrator uses a protocol that provides encrypted remote command-line access to a Linux server over TCP port 22. Which protocol is this?
A) Telnet
B) RDP
C) VNC
D) SSH
Correct: D
Explanation: SSH (Secure Shell) provides encrypted command-line access and file transfer over TCP port 22, replacing the insecure Telnet protocol which transmits data in plaintext on port 23. RDP provides graphical desktop access rather than command-line access and uses TCP port 3389. SSH also supports X11 forwarding for graphical applications and SFTP/SCP for secure file transfers.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A Windows system administrator remotely connects to a server's full graphical desktop environment over TCP port 3389. Which protocol is being used?
A) SSH
B) VNC
C) RDP
D) Telnet
Correct: C
Explanation: RDP (Remote Desktop Protocol) developed by Microsoft provides full graphical desktop access to Windows systems over TCP port 3389 and supports features like drive redirection, clipboard sharing, and audio. VNC also provides graphical remote access but uses a different protocol (RFB) and is cross-platform. RDP should be protected by MFA and accessed only through a VPN or Remote Desktop Gateway to prevent exposure to brute force attacks.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A protocol provides graphical remote desktop access and is platform-independent, commonly used to manage Linux desktops and cross-platform environments, running on port 5900. Which protocol is this?
A) RDP
B) SSH
C) VNC
D) Citrix ICA
Correct: C
Explanation: VNC (Virtual Network Computing) uses the Remote Frame Buffer (RFB) protocol to transmit graphical desktop images and runs on TCP port 5900, supporting cross-platform connections between different operating systems. RDP is Windows-specific and uses port 3389. VNC transmits data unencrypted by default and should be tunneled through SSH or VPN to protect credentials and session data.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: An organization uses a dedicated isolated server that administrators must connect to first before accessing any other internal systems, ensuring all remote management sessions are logged and audited. What is this device called?
A) Proxy server
B) Bastion host
C) Jump server
D) VPN concentrator
Correct: C
Explanation: A jump server (jump box) is a hardened, isolated server that serves as a single access point for administrators managing internal systems, centralizing all management traffic through one audited and monitored host. A bastion host is a similar concept but refers to any hardened server exposed to public networks to provide specific services. Jump servers reduce the attack surface by ensuring administrators never connect directly from the internet to internal production systems.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A network engineer needs to manage a router that is offline due to a software failure and cannot be reached over the network. Which type of access would allow management of the device in this state?
A) SSH
B) RDP
C) Out-of-band management
D) VNC
Correct: C
Explanation: Out-of-band (OOB) management provides access to network devices through a separate management network or physical console port that is independent of the primary data network, allowing management even when the device's primary network connectivity fails. SSH and RDP require the primary network to be functional and therefore represent in-band management. OOB management typically uses console servers connected to serial ports, cellular modems, or dedicated management networks on separate interfaces.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A Layer 2 tunneling protocol that encapsulates PPP frames and is commonly combined with IPSec to provide encryption for Windows VPN clients. Which protocol is this?
A) GRE
B) L2TP
C) WireGuard
D) SSL
Correct: B
Explanation: L2TP (Layer 2 Tunneling Protocol) combines the features of Cisco's L2F and Microsoft's PPTP, operating at Layer 2 to encapsulate PPP sessions, and is typically paired with IPSec for encryption in L2TP/IPSec VPNs. GRE operates at Layer 3 and encapsulates network-layer packets rather than PPP data-link frames. L2TP/IPSec is built into Windows as a native VPN option and uses UDP port 1701 for L2TP traffic with IPSec protecting it on UDP port 500/4500.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: A company wants to allow remote administrators to access a Windows environment without directly exposing RDP to the internet, using a broker service over HTTPS port 443. Which solution is this?
A) VNC over SSH
B) IPSec VPN
C) Remote Desktop Gateway
D) Jump server
Correct: C
Explanation: A Remote Desktop Gateway (RD Gateway) acts as a secure intermediary that encapsulates RDP sessions over HTTPS port 443, allowing remote access to internal Windows desktops without exposing TCP 3389 directly to the internet. A jump server requires administrators to connect to an intermediate server first but does not inherently proxy RDP over HTTPS. RD Gateway provides centralized authentication, logging, and the ability to restrict which users can access which internal systems.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: Remote management traffic that travels over the same production network as regular data traffic is best described as which type of management access?
A) Out-of-band management
B) Console management
C) In-band management
D) Air-gapped management
Correct: C
Explanation: In-band management uses the same production network paths as regular data traffic, meaning that if the network has issues, management access may also be affected. Out-of-band management uses a separate, dedicated management network independent of the production infrastructure. In-band management is simpler and less costly but creates a dependency between management access and network availability.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.4 — Compare and contrast remote access methods and security implications
Question: An organization allows remote workers to connect to internal applications only after authenticating with both their password and a hardware token. The VPN gateway enforces this before granting access. What security feature is being applied?
A) Split tunneling
B) MFA on remote access
C) Certificate pinning
D) Full tunneling
Correct: B
Explanation: Requiring MFA for remote access VPN authentication ensures that even if a user's password is compromised, an attacker cannot establish a VPN session without the hardware token. Certificate pinning validates server identity but does not add a second factor for user authentication. MFA is considered essential for any external-facing remote access service to protect against credential theft and password spraying attacks.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A data center entrance has a small enclosed room with two doors — the outer door must close and authenticate the visitor before the inner door will open, preventing tailgating. What is this physical security control called?
A) Mantrap/vestibule
B) Badge reader
C) Biometric lock
D) Security booth
Correct: A
Explanation: A mantrap (access control vestibule) is an enclosed entryway with two interlocked doors that ensures only one person can enter at a time, preventing unauthorized individuals from following authorized personnel. A badge reader alone cannot prevent tailgating because a door may be held open after the badge holder enters. Mantraps are commonly used in data centers and high-security areas to enforce one-person-at-a-time entry.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: An organization wants to verify a person's identity at a secure door using their unique physiological characteristics rather than a card they could lend to someone else. Which access control method does this?
A) Badge reader
B) PIN pad
C) Biometric reader
D) Smart lock
Correct: C
Explanation: Biometric readers authenticate users based on unique physical characteristics such as fingerprints, retinal patterns, or facial geometry, which cannot be shared or easily duplicated. Badge readers use a physical card that can be lost, stolen, or shared, making them less secure than biometrics for high-security areas. Biometric systems must consider false acceptance rate (FAR) and false rejection rate (FRR) when calibrating sensitivity for security versus convenience.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: Which physical security control uses IP cameras placed throughout a facility to record activity and deter unauthorized access, with footage available for incident investigation?
A) Motion detection sensors
B) Badge reader logs
C) Video surveillance (CCTV)
D) Alarm systems
Correct: C
Explanation: Video surveillance (CCTV) provides both deterrence and evidence collection, recording activities in physical spaces for real-time monitoring and post-incident review. Motion detection sensors detect movement but do not record visual information for investigation purposes. Modern IP camera systems with cloud storage allow offsite recording, ensuring footage is preserved even if physical recorders at the site are damaged or stolen.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: Large concrete or steel posts placed in front of a building entrance to prevent vehicles from being driven into the facility are known as what?
A) Jersey barriers
B) Fencing
C) Bollards
D) Mantraps
Correct: C
Explanation: Bollards are sturdy vertical posts designed to block vehicle access while still allowing pedestrian traffic, protecting building entrances from vehicle ramming attacks. Fencing controls the perimeter but does not stop a determined vehicle from breaking through. Anti-ram bollards are crash-rated to withstand specific vehicle speeds and weights and are commonly installed at government buildings, data centers, and high-value facilities.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A sensor system is installed in a data center that detects unauthorized entry by sensing changes in infrared radiation caused by human body heat. What is this?
A) Video surveillance
B) Motion detection
C) Acoustic sensors
D) Vibration sensors
Correct: B
Explanation: Motion detection systems use passive infrared (PIR) or microwave sensors to detect movement or changes in heat signatures, triggering alarms or recording when unauthorized movement is detected. Video surveillance continuously records but motion detection specifically alerts security staff to active movement events. PIR motion detectors are cost-effective, reliable, and commonly integrated with alarm systems and lighting to enhance physical security.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: An IT security policy requires that all laptops be physically secured to desks using a locking mechanism when not in use to prevent theft. What device is used for this?
A) USB data blocker
B) Tamper-evident seal
C) Cable lock
D) Smart card reader
Correct: C
Explanation: A cable lock (Kensington lock) physically attaches a laptop to a desk or other fixed object through a security slot, deterring casual theft. USB data blockers protect against data theft over USB connections but do not prevent physical theft of the device. Cable locks are a simple, low-cost deterrent that is particularly effective in semi-public environments like offices and conference rooms.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: An employee plugs their smartphone into a public charging kiosk at an airport and unknowingly allows malicious software to access their device's data. Which device would have prevented this?
A) Cable lock
B) USB data blocker
C) Faraday cage
D) Smart card
Correct: B
Explanation: A USB data blocker (juice jacking protector) allows power to flow through a USB connection while physically blocking the data pins, preventing data transfer during charging. A cable lock secures devices to physical objects and does not address USB-based attacks. Juice jacking attacks exploit the dual power/data nature of USB connections; data blockers ensure that public charging stations can only charge the device without accessing its files.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A company uses unique serial numbers and QR codes affixed to all laptops, monitors, and network equipment, with a database linking each tag to its assigned user and location. What is this practice called?
A) Tamper detection
B) Asset tracking
C) Change management
D) Configuration management
Correct: B
Explanation: Asset tracking uses physical labels, barcodes, or RFID tags combined with an inventory database to record the location and ownership of all hardware assets, supporting audits and theft detection. Tamper detection monitors whether devices have been physically opened or modified rather than tracking their location. Asset tracking enables organizations to quickly identify missing or unauthorized devices during audits and supports disposal and lifecycle management.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A security label on a server chassis changes appearance permanently if the chassis is opened, alerting staff that the device may have been accessed without authorization. What type of control is this?
A) Asset tracking
B) Motion detection
C) Tamper detection
D) Badge access logging
Correct: C
Explanation: Tamper detection uses physical mechanisms such as tamper-evident seals, tape, or labels that show visible signs of disturbance if a device has been opened or moved without authorization. Asset tracking monitors the location and ownership of devices but does not detect physical interference. Tamper-evident controls are commonly used on network equipment, servers, and evidence to provide a visible chain of custody indicator.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: Perimeter security that uses chain-link fencing, razor wire, and height regulations to deter unauthorized physical access to a facility grounds is an example of which category of physical security control?
A) Detection
B) Deterrence
C) Prevention
D) Compensation
Correct: C
Explanation: Fencing is a physical prevention control that creates a barrier preventing unauthorized individuals from accessing the facility grounds. Deterrence relies on psychological discouragement rather than physical barriers. Physical security controls are classified as prevention (barriers), detection (cameras, sensors), and response (guards, alarms), with fencing and locks categorized under prevention.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A company stores backup tapes and servers in locked cabinets within a data center. Even if an intruder gains entry to the data center floor, they cannot access the equipment without an additional key or access code. What type of control is this?
A) Defense in depth using physical layering
B) Motion detection
C) Video surveillance
D) Geofencing
Correct: A
Explanation: Locking server cabinets and racks inside a data center represents a physical implementation of defense in depth, requiring multiple successful breaches (perimeter, room, cabinet) before an attacker can access equipment. Motion detection and video surveillance are detection controls rather than prevention barriers. Layered physical security ensures that even a partial breach of the outer perimeter does not immediately grant access to sensitive equipment.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A security manager conducts regular training sessions teaching employees to recognize social engineering, avoid tailgating, and report suspicious individuals in the building. What is this an example of?
A) Technical security control
B) Physical access control
C) Employee security awareness training
D) Compensating control
Correct: C
Explanation: Employee security awareness training educates staff on physical and social security threats, turning employees into an active layer of the physical security system. Physical access controls like badge readers are technical/physical controls, while training is an administrative control that addresses the human element. Human error and social engineering are responsible for a large proportion of physical security breaches, making trained employees one of the most effective countermeasures.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A visitor to a data center is required to present a government-issued ID, sign a visitor log, and be escorted by an authorized employee at all times. What security concept does the escort requirement represent?
A) Tailgating prevention
B) Biometric access control
C) Defense in depth
D) Asset tracking
Correct: A
Explanation: Requiring visitors to be escorted prevents tailgating by ensuring unauthorized individuals cannot move freely through secure areas without supervision. Defense in depth describes multiple security layers overall rather than specifically the escort policy. The escort requirement combined with visitor logging and ID verification represents layered visitor management controls that are standard in data center and high-security environments.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A badge reader system records the exact time and door location for every access attempt, whether successful or denied, and stores this data for 90 days. How does this log primarily benefit security?
A) It physically prevents unauthorized access
B) It provides audit trail data for incident investigation
C) It encrypts physical access credentials
D) It replaces the need for security cameras
Correct: B
Explanation: Badge reader logs provide an audit trail that can be used during incident investigations to determine who accessed a location and when, supporting forensic analysis of security events. Physical prevention is provided by the locked door itself, not the logging function. Access logs are most valuable when cross-referenced with other data sources like CCTV footage and network logs to build a comprehensive timeline of an incident.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: A data center uses raised flooring with sensors that detect and alert security when unusual weight distribution is detected, indicating someone may be accessing subfloor cabling areas without authorization. This is an example of which control?
A) Asset tracking
B) Video surveillance
C) Tamper detection
D) Motion-based detection
Correct: D
Explanation: Weight or motion sensors detect physical presence in restricted areas, triggering alerts when unauthorized movement is detected in areas like subfloor cable runs. Tamper detection focuses on detecting whether specific devices have been physically interfered with rather than general presence in an area. Detection controls like motion sensors are most effective when integrated with response procedures that ensure alerts are promptly investigated.

Domain: 4.0 Network Security
Sub-objective: 4.5 — Explain the importance of physical security
Question: An organization requires new employees to complete a mandatory module covering physical security policies including clean desk policy, badge usage, visitor procedures, and the reporting of security incidents. What category does this fall under?
A) Technical controls
B) Preventive controls
C) Security awareness training
D) Physical access control
Correct: C
Explanation: Mandatory security awareness training educates employees about physical security policies and procedures, addressing the human element of the security program through administrative controls. Technical controls include badge readers and cameras; security awareness training ensures employees understand and comply with the policies those systems enforce.
